Since then, I have frequently encountered this condition, realizing that the pathway for food must pass from the lower right abdomen into the large intestine, a fact not widely known.

There are also methods for treating food stagnation, as indicated by pain in the abdominal area, which can be verified. Therefore, in treating accumulations, it is essential to carefully examine the causes to ensure accuracy. I have seen Danxi's discussions state that a lump in the middle indicates phlegm and fluids, on the right indicates food accumulation, and on the left indicates blood clots. If something cannot be formed into a lump, whether gathered or scattered, it is certainly qi. A lump is a tangible entity, formed from the combination of phlegm, food accumulation, and stagnant blood. I believe that what can both gather and disperse is undoubtedly qi accumulation.

If we take the left as blood accumulation and the right as food accumulation, we would be mistaken. For instance, children often suffer from accumulations that are consistently found beneath the left rib, which is merely due to overeating. Thus, would it be correct to assume that just because it is on the left, it must be blood accumulation? If we claim the left side denotes blood and the right side denotes food, could it be that the right side has no blood and the left side has no food? This should not be established as a principle.[50p]

Discourse on Governance

The classics say: what is solid must be worn away, what is preserved must be attacked, what is bound must be loosened, what is external must be removed. Things above must reach those below, things must be rubbed and bathed, things must be thinned and robbed, things must be opened and developed, appropriate methods being used for the occasion. All methods for managing accumulation, as mentioned in the classics, have already been exhausted. However, to summarize its essentials, there are merely four methods: to attack, to dissolve, to scatter, and to replenish; these four are sufficient. They are detailed as follows:

Considering all solid and concentrated energies, they cannot be eliminated without attack. For example, the secret formulas such as the Dissolving Pill, Iron Elixir, Immortal Pill, Resonance Pill, Large Salt Pill, Three Flower Blessing Pill, Red Gold Bean, and Hundred Obedience Pill are all potent attacking agents. Additionally, forms like the Triangle Pill, Winning Red Pill, Asafoetida Pill, Vitality Pill, Red Little Pill, and Warm White Pill are all lesser attacking agents.[51p]
In cases where conditions cannot withstand aggression, it is best to gradually dissipate and磨 those that are stagnant, such as He Zhong pills, Cardamom pills, Baohe pills, and various types of He Zhong drinks. If there is a buildup that does not recede and the vital energy is not depleted, one should use agents that promote the flow of qi and relieve stagnation to dissolve and subtly eliminate it. For intangible qi accumulation, it is advisable to disperse and heal it with formulas like the Air Dispelling Drink, Aromatic Spirit Powder, Zhi Mi Qi Decoction, Ten Aromatic Pills, and Four Grind Drinks.

In cases where the accumulation of qi is mild and both aggressive and supportive treatments are not suitable, one should primarily focus on regulating the spleen and stomach. For example, the Jie Gu Zhi Zhi Pill is appropriate. Additionally, I have further developed this formula and recently created a Peony and Zhi Zhi Pill, which addresses both liver and spleen to reduce swelling, eliminate accumulation, relieve abdominal pain, and improve appetite, proving to be more effective than the former.[52p]
For example, the Great Strengthening Spleen Pill, Wood Fragrance Ginseng and Ginger Pill, and other similar formulas, are all excellent remedies for tonifying the spleen and stomach, which should be chosen for use.

Generally, individuals with deficiency in the spleen and kidneys, and those who are weak and imbalanced, often suffer from conditions of accumulation. When the spleen is weak, the middle burner fails to function; when the kidneys are weak, the lower burner cannot process. When the vital energy does not circulate, pathogens can establish themselves. For such individuals, regardless of whether the issues are tangible or intangible, one should assess the urgency and always prioritize vital energy as the main focus.

For deficiencies in the spleen and stomach, it is advisable to use formulas such as Five-Flavored Differentiation Powder, Nourishing the Center Decoction, Warm Stomach Drink, or Return to Spleen Decoction. For deficiencies in the liver and kidneys, formulas like Nourishing Yin Decoction, Kidney Qi Pill, or Warming the Liver Decoction should be used appropriately; this is known as nourishing the righteous and allowing accumulation to eliminate itself. If there is stagnation present within a deficiency, it is permissible to add some adjunctive ingredients.[53p]
The key to treating accumulation lies in understanding when to attack and when to supplement, and one should discern the urgency of each situation. If the accumulation has not persisted long and the vital energy remains intact, treatment should not be delayed; for if it is delayed, it will only strengthen its hold, making it harder to control, hence this situation requires swift action. Conversely, if the accumulation has lasted for a longer period and the vital energy is gradually depleting, attempting to attack it now will be ineffective, as the accumulated energy is too distant to reach, while the vital energy is close at hand and can easily be harmed. The more one attacks, the more depleted it becomes, leading not to death from accumulation but from the attack itself. This highlights the importance of preserving life rather than focusing solely on the illness, which must be recognized. Therefore, when dealing with weakness due to evils, one should adopt a gentle approach, focusing on strengthening the spleen and stomach to fortify the foundation, using moxibustion or plasters to clear the channels. As long as the primary energy becomes stronger and the channel energy flows freely, the accumulated distention will dissipate. The balance of urgency and delay is the overall strategy. This principle applies not just to accumulation but to all illnesses.[54p]
In cases of hard masses, these must be located outside the intestines, specifically between the organs, and their resolution cannot be achieved solely through medicinal power. Therefore, it is advisable to use substances like Ferula gum resin, amber ointment, or the safflower ointment and Three Sacred ointment to attack externally, while employing the technique of the Chang Sang Jun needle to address the internal issue. Yet, such stubborn accumulations will ultimately be difficult to dissipate without the application of fire; hence, moxibustion is most effective. I have treated several patients in the capital who had hard masses in the left flank, all successfully using moxibustion.

Long-standing accumulations lead to sores due to stagnation in the meridians, which can lead to the activation of the liver, spleen, and stomach fire, causing symptoms like facial swelling, mouth ulcers, and foul-smelling gums. Therefore, externally one should use medicated plasters or moxibustion to break apart the stubborn masses, while internally one should use pills containing aloe and similar ingredients to clear the heat from the sores.[55p]
Secret Prescriptions of the Stone Chamber
By Qing Dynasty - Chen Shiduo

Treatment Method for Hard Masses

When a disease presents as a hard mass that does not easily disperse, one should use softening treatments. For instance, when a lump forms in the chest or there is accumulation in the abdomen, the method is to employ medicine to soften it. If a lump forms in the heart, this is due to the stagnation of qi and blood; thus, one should use tonics for qi and blood, adding a slight amount of ingredients to soften hard masses, allowing the qi and blood to flow, which will cause the hard mass to dissipate on its own. If one merely attacks the mass without understanding the role of warming and nourishing medicines, the hardness will ultimately persist.

The prescription includes: one qian each of ginseng, Angelica, blue salt, five-flavor herb, bupleurum, and pinellia; three qian each of white peony and ophiopogon; five qian of cooked Rehmannia; two qian of cornelian cherry; one piece of aconite, all boiled in water for consumption. This formula is excellent for its pure use of tonics, adding only blue salt to soften hard masses. If one is not focused on treating hardness, over time it will naturally soften; this is the subtle method of yielding overcoming rigidity.[56p]
The firmness of stubborn masses requires another method for treatment. The hardness lies within the abdomen; if one merely attacks the firmness, it will surely lead to disharmony in the abdomen, damaging the stomach's vital energy. Therefore, the approach should be to soften and harmonize within to treat it, allowing the nature of the hardness to ease, its form to transform, its energy to dissipate, and its blood to be consumed. Otherwise, tangible substances will take root within, while intangible energies will be exhausted externally, and over time, the firmness will remain despite efforts to eliminate it.

The formula includes five liang of white atractylodes, two liang of malt, eight liang of buckwheat flour, and one jin of turtle shell, along with three liang each of vinegar-dried white peony and poria, one liang each of pinellia, licorice, and white mustard seed, five qian each of radish seed, magnolia bark, and ginseng, along with three qian of cinnamon and one qian of aconite, all ground into powder, then formed into pills with honey. Take five qian before sleep each day, and with these fine medicines, there has never been a case of incomplete recovery.

This formula possesses remarkable efficacy, especially utilizing turtle shell as the main ingredient, which penetrates all hardness. Notably, the addition of buckwheat flour complements turtle shell to combat evils without exhausting vital energy. The other ingredients are all medicines that strengthen the spleen and regulate internal order, enabling the spleen to become robust and materials to naturally transform. The use of cinnamon and aconite as offensive reinforcements is particularly brilliant, allowing the turtle shell's forces to advance relentlessly. It symbolizes a benevolent leader; even if the enemy is strong, they would not dare to resist, scattering in fear. Additional forces follow behind, decisively eliminating without leaving a trace, integrating both suppression and pacification—who could fail to achieve victory in less than three months? This is the true excellence of softer treatment.[57p]
If the vital energy is not replenished and one only relies on Da Huang (rhubarb), Ba Dou (croton), and substances like Ai Wei (ferula), while vigorously attacking the disease, there may be temporary victories. However, the central plains will be ravaged, the fields desolate, and ultimately the granaries will be empty and the people will suffer from scarcity for years without recovery.

When someone shows signs of a lump or mass, with sudden onset and abdominal pain that cannot be touched, one can use purgative methods to expel the disorder. The formula includes one tael of bitter orange, two taels of white atractylodes, and five qian of burnt horse dung, brewed with wine for consumption. Horse dung is particularly effective at soothing pain without damaging the vital energy, and it also helps expel pathogens and transform stagnant matter, thus it is most suitable to keep it readily available in the medicine cabinet, as it cannot always be obtained in an emergency. This substance becomes more effective with age; there is no need to use it in large quantities—just one or two qian will yield marvelous results.

In this case, using five qian together with bitter orange will help dissolve the accumulated mass. However, merely dissolving the mass may hurt the spleen's yin, so adding two taels of white atractylodes will greatly strengthen the spleen's energy. Therefore, horse dung and bitter orange can work effectively to expel and disperse the condition; this is indeed a wonderful method.[58p]
Fang

Hua Kuan Wan (Danxi): Used to treat masses and blood clots. Boil 3 liang of sea powder wine, add 1 liang each of Sanleng, Pung, Honghua, Taoren, Wulingzhi, and Xiangfuzi. Add 5 qian of shijian. Grind these ingredients into a fine powder, mix with vinegar into a paste, and form into balls the size of walnuts, taking 30 to 50 balls with Baizhu decoction.

Lian Luo Wan (Rumen): Used to treat food accumulation, dead blood, and phlegm that forms masses, along with pain in the sides and disturbances akin to thunder and drum noises. Use half of Huanglian, stir-fry with 5 qian of Wuyuan, and the other half stir-fry with 5 qian of Yizhi. Then add 1.5 liang each of Baijiezi, Luobozzi, Zizhi, Chuanxiong, Sanleng, Pung, Taoren, Xiangfuzi, Shancha meat, and Shenqu. Add 5 qian of Qingpi. Grind these into a fine powder, mix with steamed cakes into balls the size of walnuts, and swallow 50 to 60 balls with clear soup. Also known as Baijie Wan, currently known as Xiaojiman Wan.

Xiao Kuan Wan (Rumen): Used to treat symptoms of masses and concerns. Use 4 liang of Dahuang, 3 liang of Nixiao, and 1.5 liang each of Ren Shen and Gan Cao. Grind these into a fine powder, place 3 sheng of aged vinegar in a ceramic container, first add Dahuang to boil, stirring constantly until boiling, then let reduce slightly to 1 sheng. Add the remaining powdered ingredients and boil until it can be formed into balls the size of walnuts, taking 30 balls with rice drink. Also known as Nixiao Wan.[59p]
Jia Wei Chai Ping Decoction: For treating accumulated heat. Ingredients: Chaihu, Huangqin, Banxia, Cangzhu, Houpu, Chenpi, Qingpi, Hawthorn flesh, Zhiqiao (roasted), Shenqu (roasted), Sanleng, and Phragmites, seven parts each; Gan Cao, five parts. Grind together to make one dose, add three slices of ginger and two dates, and decoct with water for consumption.

Xiao Ji Bao Zhong Wan: For dispersing phlegm and removing lumps. Ingredients: Stir-fried Baizhu, three liang; Juhong, two liang; Banxia, Bai Fuling, Xiangfu (vinegar-fried), and stir-fried Radish seeds, stir-fried Bai Jiezhi, Shenqu, Huanglian (ginger juice fried), and Zhi Zhi (ginger juice fried), one liang each; Boping, seven qian; Phragmites (vinegar-fried) and Sanleng (vinegar-fried), eight qian each; stir-fried Malt, six qian; stir-fried Gan Qi, five qian; Qingpi (stir-fried with fragrant oil) and Suo Sha Ren, four qian each; Mu Xiang and Asafoetida, three qian each. Grind into powder, mix with ginger juice and liquor to form pills the size of walnuts, and take eighty pills with clear soup.

Kai Huai San: For treating lumps and bloating in the chest, or heat. Ingredients: Chaihu and Caodoukou, each one qian; Sanleng (vinegar-fried), Phragmites (vinegar-fried), Qingpi, Chenpi, Banxia, Bai Fuling, Xiangfuzi, Boping, Zhi Shi, Honghua, and Gan Cao, each seven parts. Grind together to make one dose, add three slices of ginger, and decoct for consumption.[60p]
Bao He Wan: Treats all injuries and accumulations caused by food, gradually dissolving with prolonged use. Ingredients: 5 liang of Atractylodes, 3 liang each of dried tangerine peel, Pinellia, Poria, malted wheat, and hawthorn flesh; 2 liang each of Forsythia, fried Cyperus, Magnolia bark, and fried radish seeds; 1 liang each of bitter orange, maltose, and fried Coptis, as well as fried Scutellaria. Grind the ingredients into powder, mix with ginger juice to form pills the size of walnuts, and take 50 to 70 pills with warm tea.

Zi Xiang San: Treats gas accumulation in the abdomen that causes minor obstruction and may cause swelling with cold or heat. Ingredients: 1 qian each of bitter orange, earth bone bark, Pinellia, and wormwood; 7 fen each of bupleurum and Scutellaria; 5 fen each of red peony, Magnolia bark, and fragrant madder, along with Coptis and Corydalis; 3 fen of licorice. Grind the ingredients, prepare as a paste, and decoct in water for consumption.

Hua Pi Dan (from "Hui Chun"): A specific remedy for dissolving accumulations. Ingredients: 4 liang of rhubarb, soaked in vinegar for 7 days, then sun-dried and exposed to dew for another 7 days; 2 qian of safflower; 2 liang of stir-fried pangolin; 5 fen of indigo; 1 liang each of fried semiliquid gall and peach kernel, and fried Cyperus. Grind the ingredients into powder, mix the rhubarb with the vinegar to make a paste, form into pills the size of mung beans, and take 50 to 70 pills with a decoction of reed root and kudzu root.[61p]

Three-Column Pill: Treats abdominal hardness and swelling, fullness and hardness under the ribs, chest oppression, breathlessness, and shortness of breath. Regular use promotes qi flow, eliminates stagnation, and reduces swelling.

Ingredients:

  • Wheat bran: fried.

  • Green peel (Citrus reticulata).
  • Radish seeds: fried.
  • Shenqu (mixed fermentation agent): fried.
    Each of these: 2 liang.
  • Realgar powder: 1 liang.

Mix the above fine powders, combine with the ointment made from the three-column herb, and shape into pills the size of a tung seed. Take 20 pills after meals with warm rice drink.

Dew Drying Pill: Treats internal cold injury, congested qi, and lumps in the intestines leading to pain and inability to stretch the waist.

Ingredients:

  • Light powder: ground, 1 qian.

Mix the above fine powders evenly, using ginger juice to make a paste, shape into pills the size of a walnut. Take 20 to 30 pills with ginger soup or warm wine before meals on an empty stomach.[64p]

Fei Qi Wan (Fat Qi Pill) [Eastern Garden, same below]

This treats the accumulation of the liver, felt under the left rib like a cup, with a head and legs, persisting for a long time without recovery, causing cough, an obstructed feeling, and intermittent fevers that continue for years. The pulse is taut and thin.

Ingredients:

  • Chai Hu (Bupleurum) 2 taels
  • Huang Lian (Coptis) 7 qian
  • Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) 5 qian
  • Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) 3 qian
  • Jiao (Pepper, stir-fried to remove sweat and toxicity, also for closed mouths) 4 qian
  • Guang Xu (Atractylodes) 2.5 qian
  • Kun Bu (Kelp) 2.5 qian
  • Ren Shen (Ginseng) 2.5 qian
  • Zao Jiao (Soapberry, peeled) 2.5 qian
  • Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger) 0.5 qian
  • Ba Dou (Croton) (oiled removed) 0.5 qian
  • Chuan Wu (Radix Aconiti, stir-fried and peeled) 1.2 qian
  • Bai Fu Ling (Poria) 1.5 qian

Preparation:

Excluding Poria, Soapberry, and Ba Dou, grind all to a very fine powder. Separately grind Poria and Soapberry to a fine powder and mix evenly, then incorporate the Ba Dou powder and blend well. Refine with honey into pills the size of catalpa seeds.

Dosage: Start with 2 pills for the first 9 days, increase by 1 pill each day, on the second day increase by 2 pills, gradually increase until the stool is slightly loose; then add 2 pills continuously, repeating this process. Once the accumulation decreases by more than half, do not continue taking. In autumn and winter, increase Hou Po by half, totaling 1.5 taels, and reduce Huang Lian by 1.5 qian.

In case of treating wind convulsions, add Ginseng, Poria, and Shiang Pu (Acorus) 3 qian each to one ingredient, and retain Huang Lian for spring and summer at 7 qian, without reducing for autumn and winter.

Take with light vinegar soup on an empty stomach, consumed warm.[66p]
Jiajian Feiqi Pill: In spring and summer, use this formula; it is treated the same as before.

Ingredients:

  • Chai Hu (Bupleurum) 5 qian
  • Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) 5 qian
  • Ren Shen (Ginseng) 5 qian
  • Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger) 5 qian
  • Chuan Wu (Lethal Herb) 3 qian
  • Ba Dou Shuang (Physostigma Powder) 3 qian
  • Rou Gui (Cinnamon) 2 qian
  • Huang Lian (Coptis) 1 liang
  • Chuan Jiao (Szechuan Pepper) 5 fen
  • Gan Cao (Licorice) 5 fen

Mix all ingredients into a fine powder except for Ba Dou Shuang, then incorporate the Ba Dou by grinding it together until uniform. Form into pills the size of a walnut. Initially take 2 pills, increasing by 1 pill each day, and on the second day increase by 2 pills, continuing to increase until the stools are slightly loose. Then revert to taking 2 pills. Take with diluted vinegar soup on an empty stomach.

In autumn and winter, reduce Gan Jiang by 0.5 qian, double the Hou Po amount, and halve the Huang Lian amount.[67p]
Fei Qi Pill (from "San Yin")

For the Fei Qi Pill, use:

  • 1.5 taels of Angelica root
  • 1 tael of Atractylodes
  • 1 tael of Green Tangerine peel, stir-fried

  • Mix the above into a powder.

Tortoise Shell Pill

For treating Fei Qi; suitable for those who are thin and weak, with little appetite and thirst:

  • Use one tortoise shell weighing 4 taels, wash it clean, and mix with vinegar and yellow clay to bind, making it about 1 inch thick on the back; let it dry.

Additionally:

  • 2 taels of prepared Rhubarb
  • 3 taels each of Atractylodes and Myrceugenia, gently roasted to a light yellow
  • 1.5 taels each of Wood Fragrance (not exposed to fire)
  • and Peach Kernels, soaked in broth, skin removed, and finely ground to a paste.

Except for the tortoise shell, crush everything into a fine powder. Take the prepared clay and mold it onto a furnace with an opening, where the tortoise shell can be placed. Use 2 liters of good rice vinegar, infusing occasionally into the tortoise shell with the previous powdered ingredients and peach paste, simmering over low heat until thickened.

Afterward, wash the tortoise shell clean and remove the clay to bake it dry, then crush it into a fine powder and mix it with the previous ingredients, forming pills the size of Wutong seeds. Take 29 pills on an empty stomach, washed down with warm wine, and repeat before dinner.[68p]
Xibin Pill

It treats accumulation in the lung, located beneath the right rib and as large as a cup. If it lasts for a long time, it leads to chills and fever, coughing, and can develop into pulmonary abscess, with a superficial and wiry pulse.

Ingredients:

  • Thick-skinned bark (processed with ginger) - 8 qian
  • Huanglian (fried) - 1 liang and 3 qian
  • Dried ginger (炮)
  • Chuanjiao (fried to remove sweat)
  • Bai fuling (powdered separately)
  • Ziwan - 1.5 qian each
  • Ginseng - 2 qian
  • Cinnamon twig
  • Platycodon
  • Jinjian (炮)
  • Tianmendong
  • Chenpi
  • Chuanwu (炮 and split, remove skin and navel)
  • Bai doukou - 1 qian
  • Qingpi - 5 fen
  • Baduo shuang - 4 fen

Combine all ingredients, except for bai fuling and baduo shuang, and grind them into a fine powder. Form into pills the size of a tung seed, taking two pills each time.

Increase by one pill daily, and after two days, increase by two pills until the stools are slightly loose. Then revert to taking two pills. Take with bland ginger soup, consuming it far from meals. Repeat this cycle. Once the accumulation is reduced by more than half, do not take further. In autumn and winter, increase thick-skinned bark to 5 qian and maintain the previous amount (1 liang and 3 qian); decrease Huanglian to 6 qian from 7 qian.[69p]
Adding and subtracting the "Xi Ben Wan," during midsummer this accumulates as illness, causing chills and fever, shortness of breath and cough, rising qi, a thin pulse, loss of essence and blood, qi stagnation leading to shortness of breath, and blood thickening resulting in alternation of chills and heat, with cold in the qi aspect and heat in the blood aspect. The treatment method should aim to enhance the original energy, drain yin fire, and break up and reduce hardness.

The ingredients are:

  • 1 qian of Chuan Wu
  • 1 qian of Gan Jiang
  • 1 qian of Bai Dou Kou
  • 1 qian of Jie Geng
  • 1 qian and 5 fen of Zi Wan
  • 1 qian and 5 fen of Hou Po
  • 1 qian and 5 fen of Chuan Jiao (fried to remove sweat)
  • 1 qian of Tian Men Dong (heart removed)
  • 1 qian and 5 fen of Jing San Ling
  • 2 qian of Ren Shen
  • 2 qian of Gui Zhi
  • 8 qian of Chen Pi
  • 1 liang and 3 qian of Huang Lian
  • 4 fen of Ba Dou Shuang
  • a little Hong Hua
  • 7 fen of Qing Pi

These should be ground into a powder, soaked in a broth, and formed into pills the size of a tung seed. Initially take 2 pills, increase by 1 pill per day, and after two days increase by 2 pills until the stools are slightly loose. Then return to taking 2 pills, to be taken with decocted ginger soup before meals. Avoid alcohol, damp, fishy, spicy, and cold food items.[70p]
Xī Bǐn Tāng (Recipe for Relieving Phlegm)

Ingredients:

  • Banxia decoction
  • Gui Xin (Cinnamon), Ren Shen (Ginseng), Ting Li (Radix et Folium Peucedani), Wu Zhu Yu (Evodia) decoction, Sang Bai Pi (Mulberry Bark) roasted, Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) - each 1.5 qian

Preparation:
Mix these ingredients into one dose, add two sheng of water, five slices of ginger, and two red dates. Boil until reduced to one sheng, and consume before meals.

Indication:
Banxia decoction treats phlegm accumulation and alleviates coughing.

Other Ingredients:

  • Xi Xin (Asarum) without leaves and sprouts
  • Banxia (processed)
  • Jie Geng (Platycodon) roasted
  • Sang Gen Bai Pi (Mulberry Root Bark) roasted
  • Qian Hu (Peucedanum) - each 2.5 qian
  • Bei Mu (Fritillaria) without heart
  • He Li Le (Terminalia) stewed without pit
  • Chai Hu (Bupleurum)
  • Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) - each 1 qian
  • Ren Shen (Ginseng)
  • Bai Zhu (Atractylodes)

Preparation:
Crush these ingredients, take 3 qian per dose, with one bowl of water, three slices of ginger, and three red dates split open, then boil until reduced to seven parts. Strain and take warm, consuming one dose after meals and one before sleeping.[71p]
Zhi Shi San: Treats hiccuping and rebellious qi, abdominal and flank distension and hardness, coughing with blood, and sticky phlegm that is not easy to expel.

Ingredients: Zhi Shi (bitter orange) stir-fried with bran, Mu Xiang (costus), Bing Lang (betel nut), Chi Fu Ling (red poria), Wu Wei Zi (schisandra), Tian Ting Li (sweet-leafed herb) stir-fried with purple paper, He Li Luo (black pepper), and Gan Cao (licorice) lightly roasted, each in equal parts; Xing Ren (apricot kernel) one liang, soaked in water and peeled, then double-kerneled, stir-fried until yellow.

Dosage: Grind and take three qian each time, with one zhong (measuring cup) of water and half a fen of ginger, decoct until six parts remain, then strain and take warm at any time.

Fu Liang Wan: Treats accumulation in the heart, located above the navel, as large as an arm, reaching below the heart, not healing for a long time, causing distress with deep and weak pulses.

Dosage: Grind into a fine powder and make into pills the size of a walnut, taking fifty pills each time, swallowed with rice wine.

Gan Qi Wan: Treats lurking qi, horizontally lodged below the heart, hard and fixed, with chest and back pain.

Ingredients: Gan Qi (lacquer tree) stir-fried until smoke is gone, Yan Hua (milkweed) vinegar stir-fried, Gui Jia (soft-shelled turtle shell) cleaned and vinegar roasted, Nao Sha (arsenic) ground, each one liang; Mu Xiang, Tao Ren (peach kernel) peeled and stir-fried, Chuan Wu Tou (chuan woad) peeled and salted stir-fried, each half a liang; Xiong Huang (realgar) finely ground and She Xiang (musk) ground, each two qian and half.

Dosage: Grind into a fine powder, mix with other ground herbs to make a uniform paste, then vinegar-cooked into small pills the size of mung beans. Take ten pills each time with warm wine before meals.[72p]

Pi Qi Wan [Dong Yuan, same below]: Treats spleen accumulation in the epigastric region, which feels as large as a plate, not healing for a long time, causing weakness in the limbs, yellow jaundice, and inability to nourish the muscles from food, with a large and long pulse. Ingredients include Hou Po and Jiang Zhi, half a tael; Huang Lian, eight qian; Wu Zhu Yu, washed, three qian; Huang Qin and Bai Zhu, each two qian; Yin Chen (wine roasted), Suo Sha Ren, and Gan Jiang (cooked), each one and a half qian; Bai Fu Ling, ground separately; Ren Shen and Ze Xie, each one qian; Chuan Wu (cooked, skin and navel removed) and Chuan Jiao, each half a qian; Ba Dou Shuang, ground separately; Gui, each four fen. Except for Bai Fu Ling and Ba Dou Shuang, grind the remaining ingredients into a fine powder, mix in with the others, and form into honey pills the size of tung seeds. Initially take two pills, increase by one pill each day, two pills every second day, gradually increasing until the stool is slightly loose, then reduce back to two pills, taken with a mild licorice decoction, away from meals. Repeat this cycle. If the accumulation reduces significantly, do not continue taking.[73p]

Bentan Pill (from Dongyuan)

This formula treats the accumulation in the kidneys that manifests in the lower abdomen and rises to the heart, resembling a blubbering piglet. It may rise or fall without a specific time frame, persists for a long time, and causes breathlessness, weakness in the bones, and shortness of breath. It also treats men's internal issues related to the seven types of hernias and women's masses with abnormal discharges. The pulse is deep and slippery.

  • Magnolia Bark (processed with ginger), 7 qian
  • Fried Coptis, 5 qian
  • Ailanthus (boiled in wine), 3 qian
  • White Poria (ground separately)
  • Alisma, Sweet Flag, each 2 qian
  • Prepared Aconite (peeled), Scorpion, and Notopterygium, each 1 qian
  • Yanhusuo, 1.5 qian
  • Chuanwu (fried) and Clove, each 5 fen
  • Cowherb powder, 4 fen
  • Cinnamon, 2 fen

Grind the Poria and Cowherb separately into powder, then mix the remaining herbs into a fine powder. Roll the mixture into pills the size of a jujube. Initially, take 2 pills, add one pill each day, and increase by two pills every two days until the stool becomes slightly loose. After that, reduce back to 2 pills, taking them with light salted soup and having meals spaced apart.

Repeat this cycle until the accumulation decreases by more than half, and avoid further intake. In autumn and winter, increase the Magnolia Bark by half a tael, keeping the previous amount at 1 tael and 2 qian. If the accumulation is firm and large, take the prior medicine first without reducing it, and in this formulation, add 3 qian of preserved oyster, but do not add if there is hernia or abnormal discharge.

If the abdomen is full or half full, first address the source of the accumulation. The foundational medication should be taken to relieve any type of accumulation diseases for natural recovery. The same applies to all accumulations. If there is a sensation of heat, add Coptis; if short of breath, reduce Magnolia Bark; and if there is heaviness and chaos, reduce Cinnamon.[77p]

Wen Bai Wan
[From "He Ji"]
For treating accumulation in the heart and abdomen, chronic lumps the size of large cups; jaundice and retained food; morning vomiting; fullness and breathlessness; regular abdominal distension; hardness beneath the heart, causing palpitations; lateral pain in the sides; ten kinds of water retention; eight types of blockage; reversed stomach qi resulting in vomiting; food choking; five types of dysuria; nine types of heart pain; chronic indigestion from accumulated food; or persistent malaria.

Ten-Thousand Sickness Response Pill

This is made by adding Qiankang, Sanling, Gansui, Apricot Kernels, and Fangfeng, each 1.5 taels, to the original Wenbai Pill, along with 1 tael of Weilingxian and a reduced amount of Sichuan Pepper.

Thousand Gold Nitre Pill

This should be ground into blocks, avoiding causing distress; careful measurement of deficiency and excess is required.

Six taels of Nitre, eight taels of Da Huang, and three taels each of Ginseng and Licorice are used.

The above are to be ground into a fine powder, then placed in a container with three sheng of three-year-old bitter wine. Use a bamboo stick to mark increments; each person receives one sheng for one mark.

First, add Da Huang while continually stirring until it lightly boils; finish one mark, then add the remaining medicines and finish another mark, simmering over a gentle flame. Form the mixture into pills the size of egg yolks, taking one pill each time.

If larger pills are not used, make them the size of a nut, taking thirty pills per dose.

After taking, expect to expel substances resembling dark red and black matter similar to chicken liver rice gruel. Following the expulsion, avoid cold wind and rest with soft porridge.[80p]

  • Two liang of chuanxiong, boiled in vinegar and cut.

    Grind the above into a powder, mix with vinegar to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take thirty pills at a time with warm water, at any time. For severe cases, effects in one month; for milder cases, effects in half a month.

Holy Powder
Treats long-standing masses and women's blood conditions.

  • Eight qian each of realgar and rhubarb.
  • Six liang of fried wheat bran, cleaned.
  • Three liang of fried lacquer until the smoke disappears.
  • One liang each of alisma and fennel, fried.
  • One liang of areca nut.
    For women's blood conditions, add two liang of pangolin, cooked. Grind finely. Take five qian before bed, mixed with warm wine, lying on your back. This medicine affects only the heart; by dawn, expect a bowel movement resembling rotten fish guts, and red urine as verification. This medicine is non-toxic and highly effective. For children, take one qian; for those over fifteen, three qian; taking it on an empty stomach is more effective. This conforms to the ancient text; the current "Gāngmù" printed edition incorrectly lists realgar as six liang and rhubarb as eight liang, which misleads people![81p]
    Chicken Claw Sanling Pill treats internal blockages and swelling in the five organs.

Ingredients:
Chicken Claw Sanling, Shisanling, Jing Sanling, Mu Xiang, Qing Pi, Chen Pi (white part removed), each half a tael; Nüsha (realgar) three qian; Betel nut one tael; Nutmeg one tael.

Grind these into a fine powder, mix with fresh ginger juice to form pills the size of tung seeds. Take twenty pills with ginger soup on an empty stomach before lying down. Avoid all raw, cold, hard, and sticky foods.

Nüsha-infused pills eliminate accumulated masses and stasis.

For preparation: Take two pieces of black Aconite, each weighing five jiao or more. Properly seated, roast them until cracked, then remove the skin and navel, creating a jar. Add three qian of Nüsha and Mu Xiang, and one tael each of Sichuan Pepper and broken aged paper, slightly roasted under parchment.

Dissolve the Nüsha powder in one cup of water and put it in the jar, then simmer until dry, turning it into a powder. Fill the Aconite jar with this powder, then cover it with Aconite powder. The mouth should be wrapped with a mixture of white flour to a thickness of about half a finger, slowly bake over ash until evenly yellow, then remove the flour. Grind this with Mu Xiang and the rest into a fine powder.

Finally, make pills the size of tung seeds by mixing with vinegar and cooking to form a paste. Take fifteen to thirty pills with ginger soup.[82p]
Xiao Jian Wan treats accumulation of the five and six internal excesses, qi stagnation forming lumps, food accumulation resulting in abdominal distension, and emaciation due to inadequate appetite.

To prepare, soak turtle shell in vinegar for two nights, remove the skirt, and dip in vinegar again then roast until yellow; grind into powder as measured. Crush the lacquer and stir-fry until it smokes; grind into powder as measured. Grind the three-edged needle to about the size of half a jujube, soak in vinegar for two nights and roast, then grind into powder as measured. Use two and a half taels each of cinnamon (removing the coarse skin), fine soot from pine smoke (remove the glue), agarwood, dried ginger (roasted), myrrh (ground separately), radish seeds, dried scorpion (de-toxified and stir-fried), pepper, areca nut, and wood fragrance. Use five qian each of transparent natron, ground separately. Also, grind frankincense and talcum powder separately. Use two qian and five fen each of light powder.

Mix these finely ground powders well. Use vinegar to boil a thin paste and form pills about the size of small soybeans. Take twenty pills each time, taking them down with a decoction of fresh ginger in light vinegar. Take two doses daily; if no results, gradually increase the number of pills; if there’s slight efficacy, reduce the intake.

Yi Shen San dispels accumulations and helps with food intake.

For this, use one jin of dried tangerine peel, four taels of licorice, and five qian of salt.

Boil them with ten bowls of water from morning until night until they are soft; if the water dries up, add more. Dry and grind to powder, and take with light ginger decoction. For lumps, add half a tael of turmeric and cook with the previous herbs. For qi stagnation, add two taels of cyperus and cook with the previous herbs. For qi deficiency, add half a tael of agarwood and add separately. For dysentery with a closed mouth, add two taels of lotus seeds (removing the hearts) and add separately.[83p]

Aweigh Ointment: Treats all types of masses; additionally take Hu Huang Lian pills.

Ingredients: Qiang Huo, Du Huo, Yuan Shen, Guan Gui, Chi Shao Yao, Chuan Shan Jia (pangolin), Sheng Di Huang, Liang Tou Jian, Da Huang, Bai Zhi, Tian Ma – each five qian; Huai Zhi, Liu Zhi, Tao Zhi – each three qian; twenty seeds of Mu Bie Zi; a clump of hair the size of a chicken egg; Hong Hua four qian.

Preparation: Use two jin and four liang of fragrant oil, fry until black and remove the dregs, mix in hair and further fry, then remove dregs again. Gradually add Huang Dan decoction, adjusting to the right consistency. Incorporate Mang Xiao, Aweigh, Su He oil, Ru Xiang, and Mo Yao – each five qian; Mix in three qian of She Xiang until uniformly combined to form ointment for application to the affected area. For internal pills, ensure genuine Huang Dan is used.

When applying the ointment, first use (stone sulfate) nitrate, uniformly spread half a finger thick over the affected area, cover with paper, and use a hot iron to press for a long time. If the nitrate depletes, add more and continue pressing for about two hours before applying the ointment. If there is liver accumulation, add powdered aloe to the pressing mixture.

Avoid any food or drink, otherwise, the efficacy will be diminished and the parasite accumulation will not be resolved. After taking it, if there is pain in the heart and abdomen, the expelled substance will be things like fish, worms, or turtles, and only when everything is expelled by noon should one begin to consume warm porridge to stop further discomfort.

San Leng Jian: This remedy treats food-related ailments, alcohol addiction, blood clots, and qi blockages. Peach Kernel Decoction: Treats blood masses.

Grind the above into a fine powder, use a moderate amount of wine vinegar (1 medium cup), boil for three portions, add the first three ingredients while stirring continuously until it is suitable for forming pills. Then add (Shi Bu) Xie, form pills the size of tung seeds, take five pills with warm wine at dawn, and eliminate waste around noon. If not effective, repeat the dosage, and additionally use tonics for qi and blood.

Pangolin Powder: Treats masses and stagnant blood, causing pain in the heart and abdomen.

Ingredients: Pangolin (roasted), Bie Jia (vinegar-roasted), Da Huang (stir-fried), Gan Qi (stir-fried until smoke dissipates), Gui (1 liang), Chuan Xiong (5 qian), Yuan Hua (vinegar-stirred) (5 qian), Gui Wei (5 qian), She Xiang (1 qian). Grind the above into a fine powder, take 1 qian each time, mixed with wine.[97p]
Yuxian Dan: This remedy helps dispel worms and accumulated phlegm, eliminating various diseases. The ingredients are as follows: 1 pound of black and ugly head end, 1 pound of areca nut, 0.5 pound of rhubarb, 4 ounces each of sanleng and dried turmeric, and 2 ounces of costus. Grind these into a powder. Use the large soap pod to crush them into a concentrated decoction, strain the residue, and boil it into a dough to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take 40 to 50 pills, adjusting the amount based on strength, and wash them down with weak tea at the fifth watch. If not effective, drink warm tea to assist. This will help eliminate worms and accumulated harmful substances, and white porridge can be taken to restore strength.

Ganying Wan: This remedy treats food stagnation, abdominal pain, chest and stomach bloating, and vomiting or diarrhea. The ingredients include: 1.5 ounces each of costus, nutmeg, and clove; 1 ounce of dried ginger (prepared); 70 pieces of croton seeds (frosted); 140 pieces of apricot kernels (peeled and ground); and 2 ounces of powdered herbs. First, grind the first four ingredients into powder, then mix the last three together. For external use, melt 6 ounces of good yellow wax, filter it through silk, then combine it with 1 liter of good wine in a silver or stone vessel, boiling until the wax floats. Set aside for use. In spring and summer, begin with 1 ounce of fragrant oil, heat it in a pan to ripen, then add 4 ounces of wax wine, mixing until a syrup forms while hot. Combine this with the previous powder to form small pills, wrapping them in oiled paper for storage. In autumn and winter, 1 ounce and 5 dimes of fragrant oil is recommended, taking 30 pills on an empty stomach with ginger soup.[98p]
Chenmi Sanling Pill: It disperses accumulations and eliminates stagnation, addressing issues related to rice flour and grain. Use one tael of old rice, with five shelled new white beans. Slowly fry the beans over a low heat until they are charred, then remove the beans. Add two qian each of old tangerine peel, Sanling, simmered sand cardamom, malt, and one qian of southern wood fragrance. Grind these into a powder, mix with vinegar paste to form pills the size of mung beans. Take fifteen to twenty pills, swallowed with ginger soup after a meal.

Accumulation Pill: It treats symptoms related to masses and accumulations, as well as difficult-to-dissolve conditions, abdominal distension, or pain from worm accumulation, all of which can be effectively addressed without harming the vital energy. Use eight fen of沉香 (agarwood), Sanling, and galangal, all cooked with vinegar; natural copper and snake-stone, each burnt red and vinegar quenched seven times, two qian each; one and a half qian of wood fragrance; one qian and two fen each of realgar and whole centipede, eight fen of cinnabar; one qian of glutinous rice flour fried with vinegar; five fen of borneol; four qian each of aloe, resina safran, asafetida, and whole scorpion, washed and dried. Grind these into an extremely fine powder. Use boar bile to form pills, with black dog bile being especially effective; each pill should be the size of a phoenix seed. Take seven to eight fen, and up to one qian for heavier cases, swallowed with wine at dawn. When the mass is dissolved, cease taking; there is no need to finish the entire dose.[99p]
Dissolving Walnut
Wash turmeric and angelica with wine; four taels of white mustard seeds, eight taels each of litharge and saltpeter, eight taels of sea powder, four taels of rapid pulse, crushed; one hundred large walnuts. First, place all the herbs into a sand pot, boil with ample water for three or four times, then add one hundred walnuts weighing five qian each, and boil together for one day and night. Afterward, take out and dry; mix one good medicinal plaster with one qian of ferula and half a point of musk, adjust according to the size of the lump, then apply with warm hands. Before taking, consume one walnut; after three days, increase to two, then three, until complete; afterwards, use a series of Four Substance Decoction patches to cure.

Secret Formula for Divine Transformation Pill
Dissolves stubborn accumulations, breaks blood stasis, and helps expel accumulations of blood and qi. Three qian each of realgar, fried lacquer, and dragon’s blood, one and a half qian of frankincense, twenty red ladybirds with wings removed, and twenty centipedes with wings and legs removed. Grind these to a powder, mix with jujube flesh to form pills the size of peas; take one pill, up to three to five pills, before sleep, using either jujube soup, ginger soup, or safflower and tree peony soup to wash down.[100p]

Ingredients: Thunder pills, tangerine peel, peeled peach kernels, fried wheat bran, each two taels and two and a half qian. Hua Chong Wan
Ingredients: Remove soil from cicada slough, betel nut, bitter neem root, and fry with white powder, each one tael. Dried white alum, two taels and five fen.
Mix into a powder to make pills the size of tung seeds. For adults, take five pills a year, adjusting the dosage according to body size. Huang Lian Xiao Pi Wan

Musk Mallow Pill

Musk mallow, Nao Sha, Guo Gui (Cinnamon), Fu Zi (Aconite) prepared, Gan Qi (Dried Lacquer) roasted to remove smoke, Ya Zao Jiao (Soapberry), fine ink, ground frankincense, three-pronged hinge, broad herb, Da Huang (Rhubarb) fried and sifted, ground myrrh, Fu Jiang (Dried Ginger) prepared, Qing Pi (Green Peel), each one tael; Ba Dou Shuang (Castor Bean Powder) five qian. Mix all the powdered ingredients (except the ground ones) into a powder, dissolve Nao Sha in one liter of good vinegar, remove coarse dregs, slowly simmer in a silver pot over low heat. Next, add Ba Dou Shuang and Da Huang powder until a paste is formed. Incorporate the previous powdered herbs into the paste, and form pills the size of a tung seed. Take three to fifty pills with warm wine after meals.

Qing Yan Pill

Qing Yan (Green Salt), Nao Sha each one qian, Qiu Mo (Fermented Grain) three qian, forty pieces of salted soybeans, thirty each of large peppers and Ba Dou (Castor Bean), remove the skin and membrane and extract oil. Mix with thirty pieces of jujube flesh, grind evenly, make pills the size of a tung seed with vinegar as a binder. Take thirty pills with warm ginger soup. If accumulation is above, take after meals; if accumulation is below, take before meals.

Dried Persimmon Pill

Pig tooth soapberry, remove skin and strings; dried lacquer roasted until smoke is gone; ground myrrh; three-pronged hinge; Qing Meng Shi (Green Molybdenite); Fu Jiang (Dried Ginger) prepared; mercury and sand, each one qian; light powder two qian; thirty pieces of Ba Dou, remove skin and membrane, and boil with vinegar for ten boils. Grind each of these evenly, mix with soft rice to form pills the size of mung beans, coat with one qian of cinnabar, and swallow with chilled persimmon stem soup three to five pills at a time, adjusting dosage as needed. Pregnant women should not use this.[102p]

Chi Jin Dou treats various accumulations that are stagnant. For blood stagnation, qi stagnation, pain, swelling, or stubborn accumulations, this pill is especially effective. It works faster than those containing sodium nitrate, sulfur, and similar harsh substances that may harm internal qi.

Ingredients:

  • Horse chestnut skin removed, slightly oiled 1.5 qian
  • Light powder 1 qian
  • Raw aconite slightly stir-fried and cut 2 qian
  • Stir-fried soapberry until slightly charred 2 qian
  • Clove, wood musk, and tumeric each 3 qian
  • Cinnabar 2 qian

Preparation: Grind into powder, soak in vinegar, steam into pills the size of a radish seed, with cinnabar as a coating.

For gradual effects, take 5-7 pills; for immediate effects, take 10-20 pills. Consume with boiling water or decoctions of medicated ginger vinegar tea with honey and fennel. If there is excessive purging, drink one or two sips of cold water to stop. This medicine moves with heat and stops with cold.[103p]
Bai Shun Wan: Used to treat all kinds of Yang evils and accumulations, such as qi and blood stagnation, parasitic accumulation, food stagnation, and symptoms of injury from cold with heat and secretions. It is to be taken with a medicinal soup as needed, and it is beneficial in all cases.

Ingredients:

  • Chuan Da Huang (Rhizoma Rhei): one pound
  • Yacaojiao (Holographum): 1.6 ounces, lightly roasted until yellow

Prepare as a powder. Use soup to soak steamed cakes, then knead into pills the size of a mung bean. Each dose is five zhi (a weight unit) or one qian, or two to three qian, as deemed appropriate. Honey can also be used to form pills. Another name is Ba Xian Dan.

Li Yin Jian: Used to treat liver and kidney insufficiency and accumulations.

Ingredients:

  • Shu Di Huang (Rehmanniae Radix): 3, 5, or 7 zhi, or 1 to 2 liang
  • Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice): 1 to 2 zhi
  • Dang Gui (Angelica Sinensis): 2 to 3 zhi or 5 to 7 zhi
  • Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger): 2 to 3 zhi, roasted until yellow
  • optionally add Rou Gui (Cinnamon): 1 to 2 zhi

Put the above in two sheng of water and decoct until seven or eight tenths remain. Take hot.

Yang Zhong Jian: Used to treat spleen and stomach insufficiency and accumulations.

Ingredients:

  • Ren Shen (Ginseng): 1 to 3 zhi
  • Bai Bian Dou (Hyacinth Bean): 2 to 3 zhi, roasted
  • Shan Yao (Chinese Yam): 2 zhi, roasted
  • Fu Ling (Poria): 2 zhi
  • Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger): 1 to 2 zhi, roasted
  • Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice): 1 zhi

Put the above in two sheng of water and decoct until seven tenths remain. Drink warm away from meals.[104p]
Warm the Stomach Drink: Treats pre-symptoms.
Use 1-3 qian or 1 liang of ginseng; 1-2 qian or 1 liang of fried white atractylodes; 2 qian of dried tangerine peel (or omit), 1 qian of roasted licorice; 1-3 qian of fried dried ginger until scorched; 1-2 qian of angelica. Those with slippery conditions should not use this. Combine with 2 ding of water, decoct to 7 parts, and take warm away from meals.

Warm the Liver Decoction: Treats similar yin conditions.
Use 2-3 qian of angelica, 3 qian of wolfberry, 2 qian each of white poria, added costus, and fennel; 1-2 qian of cinnamon, and 1 qian of sandalwood. Wood fragrance is also acceptable. Combine with 1.5 ding of water, add 3-5 slices of fresh ginger, decoct to 7 parts, and take warm away from meals.

Minor Harmonizing Drink: Treats qi deficiency resistant to attack.
Use 2 qian each of lentils and hawthorn; 5 fen of licorice; and 1.5 qian each of white poria, dried tangerine peel, and magnolia bark. Combine with 1.5 ding of water, add 3-5 slices of fresh ginger, and decoct for consumption.

Fragrant Powder: Treats qi stagnation.
Use equal parts of clove and white cardamom (or sand ginger). Grind the two into a powder, mix with clear broth, taking 5-7 portions; for severe cases, take 1 qian without restriction on daily dosage.

To treat lumps in the abdomen, warm the internal organs, and expel three types of worms, especially for women with cold uterine blood: gather ash from mulberry branches in December, wash away the bitter juice, and sun-dry it. For every one tael of natron used, mix it with three taels of water, then blend the natron with the ash until moist. Fill a bottle half an inch with ash and place the natron inside, covering it tightly with ash. Fire it in both a gentle and strong manner until red hot, let it cool, then take it out. Spread it on a three-layered paper in a winnowing basket, pour hot water over it until the natron flavor disappears. Keep the juice in a bowl and maintain it in hot ash, ensuring the fish eyes boil until the liquid dries. Place it back in a bottle and fire it again. Take it out and grind it once more, mixing with millet flour to form pills the size of mung beans, taking five pills at a time with empty stomach wine until the illness is gone. This is called natron pills.[107p]

Translation:

For Stomach Accumulation: One liang of powdered Qian Niu, three pieces of Ba Dou powder, ground into a fine powder. Form into small pills the size of a jujube, take two to three pills after meals, followed by the appropriate medicinal broth. [Zi He]

For Removing Accumulation from Parasites: Use half a liang of black Qian Niu and two and a half qian of betel nut, ground into a powder. Take one qian, followed by a soup made with Zi Su. [From "Pu Ji Fang"]

For Men and Women with Qi Pain, Not Determined by Duration: Five liang of Wei Ling Xian, two and a half qian of fresh garlic root, half a qian of Wu Yao, one cup of good wine, one egg, simmered overnight. In the early morning, check if the eggshell is soft enough as an indication, remove the remnants, and drink warm. Use dried herbs to apply pressure, sleep on your side towards the lump. Boil the remnants again, and consume the next day. If a piercing pain is felt in the lump, this is a sign of effectiveness. [From "Zhai Yuan"]

For those with emerging symptoms and seeking to drink oil, use one liter of oil and infuse it with fragrant herbs, placed beside the patient’s head, allowing the scent to enter through the nose and mouth without drinking it. When extremely tired, sleep will occur, and the illness should exit through the mouth. Quickly use lime powder to catch it and extract it completely, indicating the onset of the illness.

If one feels a parasitic sensation in the chest and throat, often experiencing the fragrance of scallions and soy sauce, this indicates an emergence of parasitic symptoms: refrain from eating for two days, open the mouth and lie down. Use oil to fry scallions and soy sauce until fragrant, place it beside the mouth; the parasites should exit, and removing them will ensure recovery.[115p]

  • For excessive internal gas: Crush one pound of Sichuan pepper and soak it in five pounds of wine for twenty-seven days. Take one liter on an empty stomach; it is effective for the spirit.

Form balls the size of broad beans from rice; take fifteen balls with tangerine peel soup. This is named Moji Pills.

  • For abdominal masses: Mash three sheng of evodia, cook with wine, and wrap it in cloth to iron on the masses. After cooling, reheat and continue to iron until the masses move and dissipate; continue until they are completely gone.

    Accumulation of hardness in the abdomen: Mix five qian each of Asafetida and Wulingzhi, fry them until the smoke dissipates, then grind into powder. Abdominal fullness due to accumulation: Steep Guanyin willow in water overnight, then drink on an empty stomach several times before dawn; the fullness will dissipate.

For abdominal fullness that feels hard as stone and has persisted for many years: Use five sheng of Eastern branches of white poplar, remove the rough bark and finely shave it. For abdominal masses (bump resembling a turtle): Use Wuyin, fry and simmer it for consumption, along with warming the stomach and nourishing the blood with similar herbs to eradicate it. Merely relying on thunderballs or tin ash is ineffective.

Accumulation of Patterns: Use crushed yellow tortoise shell with vinegar and roast it into a fine powder, mix with one cup of cow's milk, and take one spoonful each morning.

Accumulation of Qi Blocks: Take one large soft-shelled turtle, one dou of silkworm sand, one dou of mulberry wood ash, and mix with juice for five times; cook until it becomes a paste, remove the bones and cook again to form a thick cream, then shape into pills the size of a walnut, taking ten pills each time, three times a day.

Food-Induced Cysts: For pain in the heart and abdomen, sensation of insects crawling in the throat, particularly in those with a strong desire for oily foods: take two sheng of pig lard and three sheng of wine, boil for three rounds to consume three times a day.

Spleen Accumulation and Masses: Use seven pig spleens, prick them with a new needle until broken, rub with one qian of natron, store in porcelain for seven days, and grind in iron; also take seven qian of safflower seeds, grind together, and mix with ash-free wine for consumption. One dose can cure conditions less than a year; for conditions less than five years, two doses; less than ten years, three doses.

Membrane Internal Qi Blocks: Take a pig (month-chancellor), roast it, and dip in powdered Corydalis for consumption.

Cold Accumulation in the Abdomen: With congealed food and fluids, phlegm stagnant under the heart, fullness and pain in both sides, worsening with food and drink: take one large toad, remove the skin and intestines, cut into pieces. For strong individuals, use one sheng of Glauber's salt; for average individuals, seven he; for weak individuals, five he. Boil in seven sheng of water, reducing to four sheng, and take all at once.[118p]

    Acupuncture

The "Classic of Acupuncture" states: For breathlessness accompanied by spitting blood, the point "Ju Que" is the main treatment. For abdominal accumulation moving upwards and downwards, use "Xuan Shu."

For acute pain in the heart and abdomen, as well as hernia-like symptoms, use "Yun Men." For a hardened mass below the heart, the points "Huang Yu," "Qi Men," and "Zhong Wan" are indicated.

If there's a firm mass in the upper abdomen (resembling a moon), accompanied by pain radiating to the genitals and difficulty urinating, the points "Yin Jiao" are recommended. For pain that wraps around the navel, "Shi Men" is the main point.

When the upward movement of "Ben Tun" causes abdominal pain (resembling a moon) that is severe, preventing speech, with swelling leading first to the waist and then to the lower abdomen, accompanied by firm and painful waist regions, radiating downwards, causing difficulty urinating, as well as testicular pain, "Shi Men" should be used.

If "Ben Tun" causes a cold sensation in the lower abdomen, with occasional nausea, blood in the urine, frequent urination, back pain radiating to the genitals, a feeling of urgency in the abdomen, chronic diarrhea, use "Guan Yuan." For "Ben Tun" affecting the heart, resulting in severe breathlessness, sudden weak breathing, and a feeling of faintness, with heart discomfort and loss of appetite, and if there’s a feeling of fullness with pain in the abdomen, causing violent discomfort in the lower abdomen and spine, use "Zhong Ji."

For abdominal accumulation that causes intermittent illness, "Shang Qu" should be prioritized.[122p]
Accumulation of hernia and hardness below the navel, with blood in the womb, is governed by Sijia. A hernia around the navel causes pain and, at times, rushes upward to the heart; Tianshu governs this. Qi hernia leads to belching and vomiting, with facial swelling and a tendency for a sinking feeling; Tianshu governs this.

The running piglet (bendun) rises to the ovaries, causing pain radiating to the genitalia; Guizhong governs this. The running piglet above and below is governed by Qimen. Hernia and hardness cause acute pain in the hip, radiating up and down the sides, with sharp abdominal pain and accumulation; Fushi governs this. Running piglet causes abdominal swelling; Zhangmen governs this.

Accumulation in the lower abdomen is governed by Laogong. Zhongwan governs abdominal distension and obstruction, worry and overthinking have caused damage, with Qi accumulating and severe abdominal pain leading to pus and abscesses, fluctuating up and down. Generally, if there is heat in the abdomen, with thirst and saliva production, it suggests tapeworm; press it with the hand persistently, ensuring it does not shift, then use a large needle to puncture Zhongwan and hold for a long time, if it does not move, then withdraw the needle.

The "Effective Method" states: when running piglet presents as upper Qi stagnation with heart pain that feels unbearable, urgently soak hands and feet in warm water, repeatedly changing, then moxibustion on Qihai, Guanyuan, Qimen, and Zhangmen each with a hundred strikes, and fifty strikes at Zhongji. For masses and hardness, moxibustion on the back of the ankles continuously year by year; also moxibustion on Qihai with a hundred strikes, and two hundred strikes at Zhongwan.[123p]
The "Medical Essentials" states: For symptoms of masses and accumulations, first needle the site of the mass; if severe, also needle at the head and tail of the mass, and it will respond immediately; after needling, apply moxibustion. Additionally, perform moxibustion on the Three Mile point. For accumulations, use the Middle Cavity, Suspended Pivot, Spleen Back, and Commercial Qu, and tonify; also the Cubit Marsh and Great Stream. For masses, use the Chapter Gate, Middle Cavity, Sea of Qi, Heavenly Pivot, Upper Cavity, and Communicating Valley. The "Introduction to Medicine" states: For distension masses, measure the size of the patient's big toe with a rice stalk, extend the measurement to the heel, then measure from the tip of the tailbone to the end of the stalk, opening a chive leaf width on each side. Apply moxibustion on the left side if the left is affected, and on the right side for the right. Needle three times, apply moxibustion seven times, and the results will be miraculous. Another method: at the bifurcation point of the second toe, apply moxibustion five to seven times; if the left side is affected, moxibustion on the right, and vice versa. After moxibustion, if one feels movement in the abdomen that evening, it is a verification. The "Subtle Meanings of the Jade Machine" states: In general, when moxibusting for distension, one must moxibustion at the root of the distension; there is no case where it will not be effective.[124p]
The method lies below the thirteen vertebrae of the spine, at the center of the spine, marked with ink. This is not an acupuncture point; however, on both sides of the ink mark, open three and a half inches, and by feeling with the fingers, if a slight pulse is discerned, then needle and cauterize at the point. The acupuncture point is approximately level with the navel, with more emphasis on the left side, or sometimes applying to both sides. This is the root of the distension. If the left side is affected, cauterize the right; if the right side is affected, cauterize the left, and it will also be effective.

The cauterization points: Zhongwan, Qimen, Zhangmen, Pishu, Sanjiao, and Tonggu are the points suitable for cauterization for various forms of distension. For accumulations above, it is advisable to cauterize the upper stomach, middle stomach, Qimen, and Zhangmen. For masses below, it is advisable to cauterize Tianshu, Zhangmen, Shenshu, Qihai, Guanyuan, Zhongji, and Shuidao. In all cauterization methods, it is preferable to treat from above to below. The cauterization on the navel and abdomen should be slightly more vigorous; all should first be cauterized seven to fourteen times, gradually increasing thereafter, becoming more effective with greater intensity.[125p]
The acupuncture points mentioned above can all treat bloating, so one should select and use them accordingly. However, there are cases where certain points should not be pressed, such as in the most hardened areas of bloating, whether at the head or tail, or areas that bulge or move. Instead, it is necessary to observe the channels and their origins, and one should press on the respective areas and apply moxibustion. Where the fire reaches, the hardened energy will naturally begin to disperse gradually, showcasing the miraculous effects of transformation. However, the method for moxibustion of bloating does not yield results from a single application; one must diligently select from various points and, through repeated applications—two or three times in succession—one will inevitably find relief.

For pain around the navel, with painful contraction of both testicles making it difficult to lie down, Tai Chong (Liver 3) governs this condition.

In cases of cold hernia descending to the abdomen, causing knee and waist pain like clear water, with a distended lower abdomen (some say the small abdomen), pressing up to the knee, Fu Tu (Bladder 30) governs this condition.

For cold hernia pain with abdominal bloating, weakness, and shortness of breath, Yin Shi (Spleen 6) governs this condition.

For a large hernia with a hardened abdomen, Qiu Xu (Spleen 8) governs this condition.[126p]
Inside the abdomen, there are large hernias and accumulations, which cause pain in conjunction with the yin, surging and leaking above and below. Therefore, supplement points like Shizhe, Taixi, and the cun口 of the Hand Yangming should all be fortified. The points Geyu and Yinggu govern abdominal bloating, severe pain in the stomach area, as well as muscular pain. Gaoqu governs abdominal accumulations that cause intermittent sharp pain. [Also known as Shangqu.] Si Man governs sharp pain on the sides of the abdomen. Abdominal knotting is characterized by severe pain around the navel.
