　　鱼鳖积，紫苏、橘皮、木香、姜汁。治鳖积，白马尿。　　狗肉积，杏仁、山楂。
　　虫积，雄黄、锡灰、槟榔、雷丸、芜荑、榧子、史君子。　　疟积，鳖甲、草果。

　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

　　　　　论证

　　积聚之病，凡饮食血气风寒之属，皆能致之。但曰积曰聚，当详辨也。盖积者积累之谓，由渐而成者也。聚者聚散之谓，作止不常者也。由此言之，是坚硬不移者，本有形也。故有形者曰积；或聚或散者，本无形也，故无形者曰聚。诸有形者，或以饮食之滞，或以脓血之留，凡汁沫凝聚，旋成症块者，皆积之类，其病多在血分，血有形而静也。诸无形者，或胀或不胀，或痛或不痛，凡随触随发，时来时往者，皆聚之类，其病多在气分，气无形而动也。故《难经》以积为阴气，聚为阳气，其义即此。凡无形之聚，其散易；有形之积，其破难。临此证者，但当辨其有形无形，在气在血，而治积治聚，自可得其梗概矣。[47p]

Fish and turtle accumulation can be treated with perilla leaves, orange peel, wood incense, and ginger juice. Turtle accumulation is treated with white horse urine. Dog meat accumulation can be treated with almonds and hawthorn.

Insect accumulation is treated with realgar, tin ash, areca nut, thunderbolt pills, wild yam, nut pine, and the Sage gentleman. Malaria accumulation is treated with turtle shell and grass fruit.

Discussion

Diseases of accumulation result from food, blood, Qi, wind, and cold. However, the terms "accumulation" and "gathering" need to be distinguished. Accumulation refers to what has built up gradually over time. Gathering refers to what collects and disperses intermittently. An accumulation is solid and unchanging; thus, it is termed "accumulation" (积) because it has form. In contrast, what gathers and disperses, lacking a fixed form, is called "gathering" (聚).

All tangible conditions may arise from either obstruction in food and drink or the retention of pus and blood—when fluids congeal, they lead to symptomatic masses, all categorized as accumulations, primarily affecting the blood, which is tangible and static.

Conversely, intangible conditions, whether distended or not, painful or not, arising sporadically and transiently, classify as gatherings—a category primarily concerning Qi, which is intangible and dynamic. Hence, the "Nan Jing" designates accumulation as yin Qi and gathering as yang Qi, which expresses this very meaning.

Therefore, for any intangible gathering, dispersal is easy; for tangible accumulations, dissolution is challenging. When diagnosing these conditions, one should distinguish between the tangible and intangible, whether related to Qi or blood, and the treatment for accumulation and gathering will naturally become clearer.[47p]

　　饮食之积，凡暂积者，不过以饮食偶伤，必在肠胃之内，故可行可逐，治无难也。惟饮食无节，以渐留滞者多，或痞积于左胁膈膜之外，盖以胃之大络，名曰虚里，出于左乳下，其动应衣，此阳明宗气所出之道也。若饥饱无伦，饮食迭进，以致阳明胃气，一有所逆，则阴寒之气得以乘之，而脾不及化，故余滞未消，乃并肠外汁沫，搏聚不散，渐成症积矣。然其初起甚微，人多不觉，及其既久，则根深蒂固，而药饵难及。今西北小儿多有此疾，而尤于食面之乡为最；正以面性多滞，而留疾于皮里膜外，所以不易治也。即如妇人血症气痞，或上或下者，亦多在肠胃之外，募原之间，故当以渐渐消磨求法治之。慎无孟浪欲速，妄行攻击，徒致胃气受伤，而积仍未去，反以速其危也。　　风寒外感之邪，亦能成积。[48p]

The accumulation from food and drink, when it momentarily accumulates, is merely due to dietary injuries, which must occur within the intestines and stomach; thus, it can be expelled or alleviated, making treatment not difficult. However, if one's eating habits lack moderation, leading to gradual retention, there may be a feeling of fullness in the left side of the diaphragm, because of the stomach's extensive connections known as "empty within," which emerges beneath the left breast and is responsive to clothing; this is the pathway of the Yangming Qi. If one experiences irregular hunger and fullness, with food being consumed successively, this can cause the Yangming stomach Qi to become disturbed. If it encounters cold Yin energy, the spleen is unable to transform it, resulting in lingering accumulation that combines with the fluids outside the intestines, clumping together and becoming difficult to disperse, eventually forming a condition of accumulation. Initially, this is very slight and many people do not notice it; as it persists, it takes root and becomes firmly established, making medicinal treatment difficult. Currently, many children in the northwest suffer from this condition, especially in regions where wheat is a staple; this is precisely because wheat is prone to stagnation, leaving disease beneath the skin and membranes, making it hard to treat. Similarly, women who experience blood disorders and Qi stagnation, whether above or below, often have issues outside the intestines and stomach, between the sources of the innate essence; therefore, one should gradually seek methods to dissolve it. Care must be taken not to act recklessly in haste, as doing so may hurt the stomach Qi, causing the accumulation to remain, which would only hasten the danger. Additionally, external influences of wind and cold can also lead to accumulation.[48p]

如经曰：虚邪之中人也，留而不去，传舍于肠胃之外，募原之间，留着于脉，息而成积。又曰：病名伏梁，此风根也。由此观之，凡今人以疟后成痞者，是即风寒之属，类可推矣。但疟由风寒，固易知也，而诸积于风若不相涉。不知饮食之滞，非寒未必成积，而风寒之邪，非食未必成形，故必以食遇寒，以寒遇食，或表邪未清，过于饮食，邪食相搏而积斯成矣。经曰：虚邪之风，与其身形，两虚相得，乃客其形。信乎致积之由，多由于此。即血症气痞之由，亦无出于此。然积以寒留，留久则寒多为热；风以致积，积成而证已非风。故治此者，但当治其所留，不可发散以再伤其真气也。惟慎疾者，能知所由，而虑之于始，则可为保脾之良策。[49p]

As the classic text states: The empty evil is within, lingering and not departing, residing outside the intestines and stomach, gathering between the origins, remaining within the meridians, breathing and forming accumulations. It also says: The illness is named "hidden beam," and this is the root of the wind. From this perspective, we see that people nowadays who develop a mass after contracting malaria, this is indeed related to the wind and cold, and can be inferred. However, while malaria is clearly related to wind and cold, the accumulations due to wind seem unrelated. It is unknown that the stagnation of food does not necessarily lead to accumulation just due to cold, and the evil of wind and cold does not necessarily take shape without food. Therefore, it is essential for food to encounter cold, and for cold to encounter food, otherwise, when the superficial evil has not been cleared, excessive food intake will hinder it, leading to accumulation. The text states: The empty evil wind interacts with the body's form, and the two vacuities come together, thus lodging in the form. Truly, the origin of accumulation is often due to this. Even blood symptoms and qi stagnation arise from this. However, when accumulations are retained by cold, if retained for long, cold often turns to heat; when wind causes accumulation, and the accumulation forms, it is no longer wind-related. Thus, those treating this should only focus on the area where it is retained, and must not disperse it, so as not to further injure the vital energy. Only careful patients can understand the origin and reflect on it at the onset; then they can formulate effective strategies to preserve the spleen.[49p]

　　症痞之积，凡或上或下，或左或右，本无定所。大都血积多在下，而气积食积，则上自胃脘，下自小腹，凡有留滞，无处不可停畜。余尝治一食症结痛者，乃在小腹下右角尖处，自后屡见此证，方知食道之行，必由小腹下右以入广肠，此实人所不知也。别有食停治按，在心腹痛门可考。故凡治积聚者，必当详审所因，庶得其确。尝见丹溪之论曰：痞块在中为痰饮，在右为食积，在左为血块，其不能作块，或聚或散者气也。块乃有形之物，痰与食积死血而成也。愚谓可聚可散者，此气聚无疑也。若以左为血积，右为食积，中为痰饮，则凿矣。即如小儿多有患痞者，必在左肋之下，此无非纵食所致，岂因其在左即为血积而可攻其血乎？若谓左血右食，则右岂无血而左岂无食乎？不可以为法也。[50p]

The accumulation of symptoms can manifest anywhere, whether above or below, left or right, as there is no fixed location. Generally, blood accumulates more in the lower parts, while qi and food accumulations are situated above the stomach and below in the lower abdomen. Any stagnation can potentially settle anywhere. I once treated a patient with food-related pain located at the lower right corner of the abdomen. Since then, I have frequently encountered this condition, realizing that the pathway for food must pass from the lower right abdomen into the large intestine, a fact not widely known.

There are also methods for treating food stagnation, as indicated by pain in the abdominal area, which can be verified. Therefore, in treating accumulations, it is essential to carefully examine the causes to ensure accuracy. I have seen Danxi's discussions state that a lump in the middle indicates phlegm and fluids, on the right indicates food accumulation, and on the left indicates blood clots. If something cannot be formed into a lump, whether gathered or scattered, it is certainly qi. A lump is a tangible entity, formed from the combination of phlegm, food accumulation, and stagnant blood. I believe that what can both gather and disperse is undoubtedly qi accumulation.

If we take the left as blood accumulation and the right as food accumulation, we would be mistaken. For instance, children often suffer from accumulations that are consistently found beneath the left rib, which is merely due to overeating. Thus, would it be correct to assume that just because it is on the left, it must be blood accumulation? If we claim the left side denotes blood and the right side denotes food, could it be that the right side has no blood and the left side has no food? This should not be established as a principle.[50p]

　　　　　论治

　　经曰：坚者削之，留者攻之，结者散之，客者除之，上之下之，摩之浴之，薄之劫之，开之发之，适事为故。凡治积聚之法，如经所云者，亦既尽矣。然欲总其要，不过四法，曰攻曰消曰散曰补，四者而已，详列如左：　　凡积坚气实者，非攻不能去，如秘方化滞丸、化铁丹、遇仙丹，感应丸、大硝石丸、三花神佑丸、赤金豆、百顺丸之类，皆攻剂之峻者也。又如三棱丸、胜红丸、阿魏丸、助气丸、红丸子、温白丸之类，皆攻剂之次者也。[51p]

Discourse on Governance

The classics say: what is solid must be worn away, what is preserved must be attacked, what is bound must be loosened, what is external must be removed. Things above must reach those below, things must be rubbed and bathed, things must be thinned and robbed, things must be opened and developed, appropriate methods being used for the occasion. All methods for managing accumulation, as mentioned in the classics, have already been exhausted. However, to summarize its essentials, there are merely four methods: to attack, to dissolve, to scatter, and to replenish; these four are sufficient. They are detailed as follows:

Considering all solid and concentrated energies, they cannot be eliminated without attack. For example, the secret formulas such as the Dissolving Pill, Iron Elixir, Immortal Pill, Resonance Pill, Large Salt Pill, Three Flower Blessing Pill, Red Gold Bean, and Hundred Obedience Pill are all potent attacking agents. Additionally, forms like the Triangle Pill, Winning Red Pill, Asafoetida Pill, Vitality Pill, Red Little Pill, and Warm White Pill are all lesser attacking agents.[51p]

　　凡不堪攻击，止宜消导渐磨者，如和中丸、草豆蔻丸、保和丸、大小和中饮之类是也。若积聚下之不退而元气未亏者，但当以行气开滞等剂，融化而潜消之。无形气聚，宜散而愈者，如排气饮、神香散、指迷七气汤、十香丸、四磨饮之属是也。　　凡积痞势缓，而攻补俱有未便者，当专以调理脾胃为主，如洁古之枳朮丸，乃其宜也。余复因其方而推广之，近制芍药枳朮丸，兼肝脾以消膨胀，除积聚，止腹痛，进饮食，用缓收功，其效殊胜于彼。[52p]

In cases where conditions cannot withstand aggression, it is best to gradually dissipate and磨 those that are stagnant, such as He Zhong pills, Cardamom pills, Baohe pills, and various types of He Zhong drinks. If there is a buildup that does not recede and the vital energy is not depleted, one should use agents that promote the flow of qi and relieve stagnation to dissolve and subtly eliminate it. For intangible qi accumulation, it is advisable to disperse and heal it with formulas like the Air Dispelling Drink, Aromatic Spirit Powder, Zhi Mi Qi Decoction, Ten Aromatic Pills, and Four Grind Drinks.

In cases where the accumulation of qi is mild and both aggressive and supportive treatments are not suitable, one should primarily focus on regulating the spleen and stomach. For example, the Jie Gu Zhi Zhi Pill is appropriate. Additionally, I have further developed this formula and recently created a Peony and Zhi Zhi Pill, which addresses both liver and spleen to reduce swelling, eliminate accumulation, relieve abdominal pain, and improve appetite, proving to be more effective than the former.[52p]

再如大健脾丸、木香人参生姜枳朮丸，皆调补脾胃之妙剂，所当择用者也。　　凡脾肾不足，及虚弱失调之人，多有积聚之病。盖脾虚则中焦不运，肾虚则下焦不化，正气不行，则邪滞得以居之。若此辈者，无论其有形无形，但当察其缓急，皆以正气为主。凡虚在脾胃者，宜五味异功散，或养中煎、温胃饮、归脾汤之类主之。虚在肝肾者，宜理阴煎、肾气丸、暖肝煎之类，酌而用之，此所谓养正积自除也。其或虚中有滞者，则不妨少加佐使。[53p]

For example, the Great Strengthening Spleen Pill, Wood Fragrance Ginseng and Ginger Pill, and other similar formulas, are all excellent remedies for tonifying the spleen and stomach, which should be chosen for use.

Generally, individuals with deficiency in the spleen and kidneys, and those who are weak and imbalanced, often suffer from conditions of accumulation. When the spleen is weak, the middle burner fails to function; when the kidneys are weak, the lower burner cannot process. When the vital energy does not circulate, pathogens can establish themselves. For such individuals, regardless of whether the issues are tangible or intangible, one should assess the urgency and always prioritize vital energy as the main focus.

For deficiencies in the spleen and stomach, it is advisable to use formulas such as Five-Flavored Differentiation Powder, Nourishing the Center Decoction, Warm Stomach Drink, or Return to Spleen Decoction. For deficiencies in the liver and kidneys, formulas like Nourishing Yin Decoction, Kidney Qi Pill, or Warming the Liver Decoction should be used appropriately; this is known as nourishing the righteous and allowing accumulation to eliminate itself. If there is stagnation present within a deficiency, it is permissible to add some adjunctive ingredients.[53p]

　　治积之要，在知攻补之宜，而攻补之宜，当于孰缓孰急中辨之。凡积聚未久而元气未损者，治不宜缓，盖缓之则养成其势，反以难制，此其所急，在速攻可也。若积聚渐久，元气日虚，此而攻之，则积气本远，攻不易及，胃气切近，先受其伤，愈攻愈虚，则不死于积而死于攻矣。此其所重在命，不在乎病，所当察也。故凡治虚邪者，当从缓治，只宜专培脾胃以固其本，或灸或膏以疏其经，但使主气日强，经气日通，则积痞自消。缓急之机，即万全之策也。不独治积，诸病亦然。[54p]

The key to treating accumulation lies in understanding when to attack and when to supplement, and one should discern the urgency of each situation. If the accumulation has not persisted long and the vital energy remains intact, treatment should not be delayed; for if it is delayed, it will only strengthen its hold, making it harder to control, hence this situation requires swift action. Conversely, if the accumulation has lasted for a longer period and the vital energy is gradually depleting, attempting to attack it now will be ineffective, as the accumulated energy is too distant to reach, while the vital energy is close at hand and can easily be harmed. The more one attacks, the more depleted it becomes, leading not to death from accumulation but from the attack itself. This highlights the importance of preserving life rather than focusing solely on the illness, which must be recognized. Therefore, when dealing with weakness due to evils, one should adopt a gentle approach, focusing on strengthening the spleen and stomach to fortify the foundation, using moxibustion or plasters to clear the channels. As long as the primary energy becomes stronger and the channel energy flows freely, the accumulated distention will dissipate. The balance of urgency and delay is the overall strategy. This principle applies not just to accumulation but to all illnesses.[54p]

　　凡坚痞之积，必在肠胃之外，募原之间，原非药力所能猝至，宜用阿魏膏、琥珀膏或水红花膏、三圣膏之类以攻其外，再用长桑君针法以攻其内，然此坚顽之积，非用火攻，终难消散，故莫妙于灸。余在燕都尝治愈痞块在左胁者数人，皆以灸法收功。　　积久成疳，乃其经络壅滞，致动肝脾阳明之火，故为颊肿口糜牙龈臭烂之证，此其在外当用膏药艾火以破坚顽，在内当用芦荟等丸以清疳热。[55p]

In cases of hard masses, these must be located outside the intestines, specifically between the organs, and their resolution cannot be achieved solely through medicinal power. Therefore, it is advisable to use substances like Ferula gum resin, amber ointment, or the safflower ointment and Three Sacred ointment to attack externally, while employing the technique of the Chang Sang Jun needle to address the internal issue. Yet, such stubborn accumulations will ultimately be difficult to dissipate without the application of fire; hence, moxibustion is most effective. I have treated several patients in the capital who had hard masses in the left flank, all successfully using moxibustion.

Long-standing accumulations lead to sores due to stagnation in the meridians, which can lead to the activation of the liver, spleen, and stomach fire, causing symptoms like facial swelling, mouth ulcers, and foul-smelling gums. Therefore, externally one should use medicated plasters or moxibustion to break apart the stubborn masses, while internally one should use pills containing aloe and similar ingredients to clear the heat from the sores.[55p]

　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

　　　　　痞块治法

　　病有坚劲而不肯轻易散者，当用软治。如人生块于胸中，积痞于腹内，法用药以软之，心中生块，此气血坚凝之故，法当用补血补气之中，少加软坚之味，则气血活而坚块自消。倘徒攻其块，而不知温补之药，则坚终不得消。方用人参、当归、青盐、五味、柴胡、半夏各一钱，白芍、麦冬各三钱，熟地五钱，山茱萸二钱，附子一片，水煎服。此方妙在纯用补药，止加青盐一味以软坚，若无意于治坚者，久之而坚自软，此柔能制刚之妙法也。[56p]

Secret Prescriptions of the Stone Chamber
By Qing Dynasty - Chen Shiduo

Treatment Method for Hard Masses

When a disease presents as a hard mass that does not easily disperse, one should use softening treatments. For instance, when a lump forms in the chest or there is accumulation in the abdomen, the method is to employ medicine to soften it. If a lump forms in the heart, this is due to the stagnation of qi and blood; thus, one should use tonics for qi and blood, adding a slight amount of ingredients to soften hard masses, allowing the qi and blood to flow, which will cause the hard mass to dissipate on its own. If one merely attacks the mass without understanding the role of warming and nourishing medicines, the hardness will ultimately persist.

The prescription includes: one qian each of ginseng, Angelica, blue salt, five-flavor herb, bupleurum, and pinellia; three qian each of white peony and ophiopogon; five qian of cooked Rehmannia; two qian of cornelian cherry; one piece of aconite, all boiled in water for consumption. This formula is excellent for its pure use of tonics, adding only blue salt to soften hard masses. If one is not focused on treating hardness, over time it will naturally soften; this is the subtle method of yielding overcoming rigidity.[56p]

痞块之坚，又一法以治之。盖坚在于腹中，若徒攻其坚，必致腹中不和，而损伤胃气，法当用和解之中软以治之，则坚之性可缓，而坚之形可化，坚之气可溃，坚之血可消。否则有形之物，盘踞于中，无形之气，必耗于外，日除坚而坚终不得去也。方用白朮五两，神曲二两，地栗粉八两，鳖甲一斤酢炙白芍、茯苓各三两，半夏、甘草、白芥子各一两，萝卜子、厚朴、人参各五钱，肉桂三钱，附子一钱各为末，蜜为丸，每日临睡送下五钱，即以美物压之，一料未有不全愈者。
此方有神功，妙在用鳖甲为君，则无坚不入，尤妙用地栗粉佐鳖甲以攻邪，又不耗散真气；其余各品，俱是健脾理正之药，则脾健而物自化。尤妙用肉桂、附子冲锋，突围而进，则鳖甲大军相继而入，勇不可当。又是仁者之师，贼虽强横，自不敢抵敌，望风披靡散走。又有诸军在后，斩杀无遗，剿抚并用，有不三月告捷者哉？此更软治之妙。[57p]

The firmness of stubborn masses requires another method for treatment. The hardness lies within the abdomen; if one merely attacks the firmness, it will surely lead to disharmony in the abdomen, damaging the stomach's vital energy. Therefore, the approach should be to soften and harmonize within to treat it, allowing the nature of the hardness to ease, its form to transform, its energy to dissipate, and its blood to be consumed. Otherwise, tangible substances will take root within, while intangible energies will be exhausted externally, and over time, the firmness will remain despite efforts to eliminate it.

The formula includes five liang of white atractylodes, two liang of malt, eight liang of buckwheat flour, and one jin of turtle shell, along with three liang each of vinegar-dried white peony and poria, one liang each of pinellia, licorice, and white mustard seed, five qian each of radish seed, magnolia bark, and ginseng, along with three qian of cinnamon and one qian of aconite, all ground into powder, then formed into pills with honey. Take five qian before sleep each day, and with these fine medicines, there has never been a case of incomplete recovery.

This formula possesses remarkable efficacy, especially utilizing turtle shell as the main ingredient, which penetrates all hardness. Notably, the addition of buckwheat flour complements turtle shell to combat evils without exhausting vital energy. The other ingredients are all medicines that strengthen the spleen and regulate internal order, enabling the spleen to become robust and materials to naturally transform. The use of cinnamon and aconite as offensive reinforcements is particularly brilliant, allowing the turtle shell's forces to advance relentlessly. It symbolizes a benevolent leader; even if the enemy is strong, they would not dare to resist, scattering in fear. Additional forces follow behind, decisively eliminating without leaving a trace, integrating both suppression and pacification—who could fail to achieve victory in less than three months? This is the true excellence of softer treatment.[57p]

倘不补正气，惟大黄、巴豆两头尖、阿魏之类，直前攻坚，虽亦有得胜之时，然中州扫荡，田野萧然，终必仓空箱罄，人民匮乏之形，有数年不能培植者也。　　有人成痞块之证，一时发作，而腹痛不可手按者，可用下堕之法，盖乘其邪动而堕之也。方用枳实一两，白朮二两，马粪炒焦五钱，酒煎服。盖马粪最能安痛，又不伤气，且又能逐邪而化物，故药笼中最宜预备之，盖仓猝间不可即得。此物愈久愈妙，不必多用至五钱，即一二钱用之，无不奇妙。今用五钱又与枳实同用，则积块自消。然而徒消其积，未免恐伤脾阴，又佐以白朮二两，大健其脾气，则马粪与枳实，可以施其祛荡之功，此妙法也。[58p]

If the vital energy is not replenished and one only relies on Da Huang (rhubarb), Ba Dou (croton), and substances like Ai Wei (ferula), while vigorously attacking the disease, there may be temporary victories. However, the central plains will be ravaged, the fields desolate, and ultimately the granaries will be empty and the people will suffer from scarcity for years without recovery.

When someone shows signs of a lump or mass, with sudden onset and abdominal pain that cannot be touched, one can use purgative methods to expel the disorder. The formula includes one tael of bitter orange, two taels of white atractylodes, and five qian of burnt horse dung, brewed with wine for consumption. Horse dung is particularly effective at soothing pain without damaging the vital energy, and it also helps expel pathogens and transform stagnant matter, thus it is most suitable to keep it readily available in the medicine cabinet, as it cannot always be obtained in an emergency. This substance becomes more effective with age; there is no need to use it in large quantities—just one or two qian will yield marvelous results.

In this case, using five qian together with bitter orange will help dissolve the accumulated mass. However, merely dissolving the mass may hurt the spleen's yin, so adding two taels of white atractylodes will greatly strengthen the spleen's energy. Therefore, horse dung and bitter orange can work effectively to expel and disperse the condition; this is indeed a wonderful method.[58p]

　　化块丸 【丹溪】 　治痞块及血块。　　海粉酒煮　三棱　蓬朮俱酢煮　红花　桃仁　五灵脂　香附子各一两　石碱五钱　　右为末，酢糊和丸梧子大，白朮汤下三五十丸。
　　连萝丸 【《入门》】 　治食积死血，痰饮成块，两胁作痛，雷鸣嘈杂眩运。　　黄连一半，以吴萸五钱同炒，一半以益智五钱同炒，去吴萸、益智　白芥子炒　萝卜子炒，各一两半　栀子　川芎　三棱　蓬朮　桃仁　香附子　山楂肉　神曲各一两　青皮五钱　　右为末，蒸饼和丸梧子大，白汤吞下五六十丸。一名白芥丸，今名消积丸。
　　消块丸 【《入门》】 　治痞块症瘕。　　大黄四两　硝石三两　人参　甘草各一两五钱　　右为末，陈酢三升，置磁器内，先纳大黄煎，不住手搅，使沸，微尽一升，下余药末，熬至可丸，则丸梧子大，米饮下三十丸，当利如鸡肝恶物。一名硝石丸。[59p]

Fang

Hua Kuan Wan (Danxi): Used to treat masses and blood clots. Boil 3 liang of sea powder wine, add 1 liang each of Sanleng, Pung, Honghua, Taoren, Wulingzhi, and Xiangfuzi. Add 5 qian of shijian. Grind these ingredients into a fine powder, mix with vinegar into a paste, and form into balls the size of walnuts, taking 30 to 50 balls with Baizhu decoction.

Lian Luo Wan (Rumen): Used to treat food accumulation, dead blood, and phlegm that forms masses, along with pain in the sides and disturbances akin to thunder and drum noises. Use half of Huanglian, stir-fry with 5 qian of Wuyuan, and the other half stir-fry with 5 qian of Yizhi. Then add 1.5 liang each of Baijiezi, Luobozzi, Zizhi, Chuanxiong, Sanleng, Pung, Taoren, Xiangfuzi, Shancha meat, and Shenqu. Add 5 qian of Qingpi. Grind these into a fine powder, mix with steamed cakes into balls the size of walnuts, and swallow 50 to 60 balls with clear soup. Also known as Baijie Wan, currently known as Xiaojiman Wan.

Xiao Kuan Wan (Rumen): Used to treat symptoms of masses and concerns. Use 4 liang of Dahuang, 3 liang of Nixiao, and 1.5 liang each of Ren Shen and Gan Cao. Grind these into a fine powder, place 3 sheng of aged vinegar in a ceramic container, first add Dahuang to boil, stirring constantly until boiling, then let reduce slightly to 1 sheng. Add the remaining powdered ingredients and boil until it can be formed into balls the size of walnuts, taking 30 balls with rice drink. Also known as Nixiao Wan.[59p]

　　加味柴平汤 【《回春》】 　治积块有热。　　柴胡　黄芩　半夏　苍朮　厚朴　陈皮　青皮　山楂肉　枳壳炒　神曲炒　三棱　蓬朮各七分　甘草五分　　右銼，作一贴，入姜三片，枣二枚，水煎服。
　　消积保中丸 【《医鉴》，下同】 　散痞除块。　　白朮土炒，三两　橘红二两　半夏　白茯苓　香附酢炒　萝卜子炒　白芥子炒　神曲炒　黄连姜汁炒　栀子姜汁炒，各一两　槟榔七钱　蓬朮酢炒　三棱酢炒，各八钱　麦芽炒，六钱　干漆炒，五钱　青皮香油炒　缩砂仁各四钱　木香　阿魏各三钱　　右为末，以姜汁酒糊和丸梧子大，白汤下八十丸。
　　开怀散　治心下积块痞闷，或发热。　　柴胡　草豆蔻各一钱　三棱酢炒　蓬朮酢炒　青皮　陈皮　半夏　白茯苓　香附子　槟榔　枳实　红花　甘草各七分　　右銼，作一贴，姜三片，煎服。[60p]

Jia Wei Chai Ping Decoction: For treating accumulated heat. Ingredients: Chaihu, Huangqin, Banxia, Cangzhu, Houpu, Chenpi, Qingpi, Hawthorn flesh, Zhiqiao (roasted), Shenqu (roasted), Sanleng, and Phragmites, seven parts each; Gan Cao, five parts. Grind together to make one dose, add three slices of ginger and two dates, and decoct with water for consumption.

Xiao Ji Bao Zhong Wan: For dispersing phlegm and removing lumps. Ingredients: Stir-fried Baizhu, three liang; Juhong, two liang; Banxia, Bai Fuling, Xiangfu (vinegar-fried), and stir-fried Radish seeds, stir-fried Bai Jiezhi, Shenqu, Huanglian (ginger juice fried), and Zhi Zhi (ginger juice fried), one liang each; Boping, seven qian; Phragmites (vinegar-fried) and Sanleng (vinegar-fried), eight qian each; stir-fried Malt, six qian; stir-fried Gan Qi, five qian; Qingpi (stir-fried with fragrant oil) and Suo Sha Ren, four qian each; Mu Xiang and Asafoetida, three qian each. Grind into powder, mix with ginger juice and liquor to form pills the size of walnuts, and take eighty pills with clear soup.

Kai Huai San: For treating lumps and bloating in the chest, or heat. Ingredients: Chaihu and Caodoukou, each one qian; Sanleng (vinegar-fried), Phragmites (vinegar-fried), Qingpi, Chenpi, Banxia, Bai Fuling, Xiangfuzi, Boping, Zhi Shi, Honghua, and Gan Cao, each seven parts. Grind together to make one dose, add three slices of ginger, and decoct for consumption.[60p]

　　保和丸　治一切饮食所伤及积聚痞块，久服自消。　　白朮五两　陈皮　半夏　茯苓　神曲炒　山楂肉各三两　连翘　香附子酒炒　厚朴　萝卜子炒，各二两　枳实　麦芽　黄连酒炒　黄芩酒炒，各一两　　右为末，姜汁糊和丸梧子大，茶清下五七十丸。

　　化痞丹 【《回春》】 　消积块专攻之剂。　　大黄四两，酢浸七日，日晒夜露七日　红花二钱　穿山甲炒，二两　青黛五分　木鳖子去油　桃仁　香附子便浸炒，各一两　　右为末，将大黄和好酢煮为糊，和丸菉豆大，茅根葛根煎汤，下五七十丸。[61p]

Bao He Wan: Treats all injuries and accumulations caused by food, gradually dissolving with prolonged use. Ingredients: 5 liang of Atractylodes, 3 liang each of dried tangerine peel, Pinellia, Poria, malted wheat, and hawthorn flesh; 2 liang each of Forsythia, fried Cyperus, Magnolia bark, and fried radish seeds; 1 liang each of bitter orange, maltose, and fried Coptis, as well as fried Scutellaria. Grind the ingredients into powder, mix with ginger juice to form pills the size of walnuts, and take 50 to 70 pills with warm tea.

Zi Xiang San: Treats gas accumulation in the abdomen that causes minor obstruction and may cause swelling with cold or heat. Ingredients: 1 qian each of bitter orange, earth bone bark, Pinellia, and wormwood; 7 fen each of bupleurum and Scutellaria; 5 fen each of red peony, Magnolia bark, and fragrant madder, along with Coptis and Corydalis; 3 fen of licorice. Grind the ingredients, prepare as a paste, and decoct in water for consumption.

Hua Pi Dan (from "Hui Chun"): A specific remedy for dissolving accumulations. Ingredients: 4 liang of rhubarb, soaked in vinegar for 7 days, then sun-dried and exposed to dew for another 7 days; 2 qian of safflower; 2 liang of stir-fried pangolin; 5 fen of indigo; 1 liang each of fried semiliquid gall and peach kernel, and fried Cyperus. Grind the ingredients into powder, mix the rhubarb with the vinegar to make a paste, form into pills the size of mung beans, and take 50 to 70 pills with a decoction of reed root and kudzu root.[61p]

　　增损五积丸　通治五积。
　　黄连肝积五钱，脾肾积七钱，心肺积一两五钱　厚朴肝心肺积五钱，脾肾积八钱　川乌头肝肺积一钱，心肾脾积五分　干姜肝心积五分，肺脾肾积一钱五分　人参肝心脾肺积二钱，肾积五分　茯苓一钱五分　巴豆霜五分　　右为末，蜜丸梧子大，初服二丸，渐加，以微溏为度。治积块不拘脐上下左右通用。如肝积，加柴胡一两，川椒四钱，蓬朮三钱，皂角、昆布各二钱五分。心积，加黄芩三钱，肉桂、茯神、丹参各一钱，菖蒲五分。肺积，加桔梗三棱，天门冬、青皮、陈皮、白豆蔻各一钱，紫菀、川椒各一钱五分。脾积，加吴茱萸、黄芩、缩砂各二钱，泽泻、茵陈各一钱，川椒五分。肾积，加延胡索三钱，苦楝肉、全蝎、附子、独活各一钱，泽泻、菖蒲各二钱，肉桂三分，丁香五分。[62p]

Increased and Reduced Five Accumulation Pills Treat All Five Accumulations

For bile accumulation: Huang Lian (Coptis) 5 qian, spleen and kidney accumulation: 7 qian, heart and lung accumulation: 1 liang and 5 qian. For liver, heart, and lung accumulation: Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) 5 qian, spleen and kidney accumulation: 8 qian. For liver and lung accumulation: Chuan Wu Tou (Aconite) 1 qian, heart, kidney, and spleen accumulation: 5 fen. For liver and heart accumulation: Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger) 5 fen, lung, spleen, and kidney accumulation: 1 qian and 5 fen. For liver, heart, spleen, and lung accumulation: Ren Shen (Ginseng) 2 qian, kidney accumulation: 5 fen. For Fu Ling (Poria) 1 qian and 5 fen and Ba Dou Shuang (Ricinus Powder) 5 fen, mix these into a powder, form into honey pills the size of a wutong seed. Initially take 2 pills, gradually increase, aiming for a slight looseness of the bowels. This treats accumulations regardless of position—upper, lower, left, or right.

For liver accumulation, add 1 liang of Chai Hu (Bupleurum), 4 qian of Chuan Jiao (Sichuan Pepper), 3 qian of Peng Zhu (Atractylodes), and 2 qian and 5 fen each of Zao Jiao (Soapberry) and Kun Bu (Kelp).

For heart accumulation, add 3 qian of Huang Qin (Skullcap), 1 qian each of Rou Gui (Cinnamon), Fu Shen (Poria's Root), and Dan Shen (Salvia), and 5 fen of Chao Pu (Acorus).

For lung accumulation, add 3 qian of Jie Geng (Platycodon), 1 qian each of Tian Men Dong (Asparagus), Qing Pi (Green Citrus Peel), Chen Pi (Aged Tangerine Peel), and Bai Dou Kou (Cardamom), and 1 qian and 5 fen each of Zi Wan (Aster) and Chuan Jiao.

For spleen accumulation, add 2 qian each of Wu Zhu Yu (Evodia), Huang Qin, and Suo Sha (Fructus), 1 qian each of Ze Xie (Alisma) and Yin Chen (Artemisia), and 5 fen of Chuan Jiao.

For kidney accumulation, add 3 qian of Yan Hu Suo (Corydalis), 1 qian each of Ku Lian Rou (Melia), Quan Xie (Scorpion), Fu Zi (Aconite), and Du Huo (Angelica), 2 qian each of Ze Xie and Chao Pu, 3 fen of Rou Gui, and 5 fen of Ding Xiang (Clove).[62p]

　　三棱煎丸　治心腹坚胀，胁下满硬，胸中痞塞，喘满短气，常服顺气，消积滞，除膨胀。　　三棱生半斤，捣为末，以酒三升，于银石器内熬膏　杏仁去皮尖炒　干漆炒烟尽　麦糵炒，各三两　青皮　萝卜子炒　神曲炒，各二两　硇砂飞，一两　　右为细末，以三棱膏和丸如桐子大，每服二十丸，食后温米饮送下。
　　晞露丸 【《宝鉴》，下同】 　治寒伤于内，气凝不流，结于肠外，久为症瘕，时作疼痛，腰不得伸。　　三棱　莪朮各一两，并酒浸入巴豆三十粒，切碎同炒深黄，去巴豆　川乌炮　干漆炒烟尽，各五钱　茴香盐炒　青皮　穿山甲炒　雄黄研，各三钱　硇砂研，四钱　轻粉研，一钱　麝香另研，五分　　右为细末，研匀，姜汁煮面糊，和丸梧子大，每服二十丸至三十丸，姜汤送下，温酒亦得，空心食前。[64p]

Three-Column Pill: Treats abdominal hardness and swelling, fullness and hardness under the ribs, chest oppression, breathlessness, and shortness of breath. Regular use promotes qi flow, eliminates stagnation, and reduces swelling.

Ingredients:

  • Three-Column (Sannong) herb: 0.5 jin (Chinese pounds), crushed to powder.
  • Alcohol: 3 sheng (Chinese liters), used to concoct an ointment in a silver vessel.
  • Almonds: peeled and fried.
  • Dry lacquer: fried until smoke dissipates.
  • Wheat bran: fried.
    Each of these: 3 liang (Chinese taels).
  • Green peel (Citrus reticulata).
  • Radish seeds: fried.
  • Shenqu (mixed fermentation agent): fried.
    Each of these: 2 liang.
  • Realgar powder: 1 liang.

Mix the above fine powders, combine with the ointment made from the three-column herb, and shape into pills the size of a tung seed. Take 20 pills after meals with warm rice drink.

Dew Drying Pill: Treats internal cold injury, congested qi, and lumps in the intestines leading to pain and inability to stretch the waist.

Ingredients:

  • Three-Column (Sannong) herb: 1 liang.
  • Atractylodes: 1 liang. Soak with 30 seeds of croton for deep frying until golden, then remove croton.
  • Chuanwu (prepared Aconitum): fried until smoke dissipates.
  • Fennel: fried with salt.
  • Green peel.
  • Pangolin scales: fried.
  • Realgar powder: ground, each 3 qian (Chinese ounces).
  • Nanjing sand: ground, 4 qian.
  • Light powder: ground, 1 qian.
  • Musk: ground separately, 5 fen (1/10 of a qian).

Mix the above fine powders evenly, using ginger juice to make a paste, shape into pills the size of a walnut. Take 20 to 30 pills with ginger soup or warm wine before meals on an empty stomach.[64p]

　　木香通气散　治寒气结瘕，腹大坚满，痛不可忍。　　木香　戎盐炒　荆三棱炮，各五钱　枳实麸炒　炙甘草各三钱　厚朴姜炙，一两　干姜炮　蓬朮炮，各二钱　　右为末，每服三钱，淡生姜汤食前调下。
　　见晛丸　治寒客下焦，血气闭塞而成瘕聚，坚大久不消者。　　附子炮去皮脐，四钱　鬼箭羽　紫石英各三钱　泽泻　肉桂　延胡索　木香　大黄用酒同三棱浸一宿，焙，各二钱　三棱五钱　槟榔二钱五分　水蛭一钱，炒烟尽　桃仁三十粒，去皮尖，麸炒研　血竭另研，一钱五分　　右十三味，除血竭、桃仁外同为末，入另研二味和匀，用元浸药酒打糊，丸如桐子大，每服三十丸，淡酢汤送下，食前温酒亦得。[65p]

Mudan Tongqi Powder: Treats the accumulation of cold and qi, with a distended, firm abdomen and unbearable pain.

Ingredients:

  • Mu Xiang (Wood Fragrance) - 5 qian, fried with Rong salt
  • Jing Sanleng (Three-edged Needles) - 5 qian, roasted
  • Zhi Shi (Bitter Orange) - 3 qian, fried
  • Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) - 3 qian
  • Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) - 1 liang, roasted with ginger
  • Gan Jiang (Dry Ginger) - 2 qian, roasted
  • Feng Zhu (Pungent Wormwood) - 2 qian, roasted

Grind these into a powder; take 3 qian with light fresh ginger soup before meals.

Jian Xian Pill: Treats cold invading the lower body, with stagnant blood and qi leading to firm masses that have not dissipated for a long time.

Ingredients:

  • Fu Zi (Aconite) - 4 qian, roasted, peeled and pitted
  • Gui Jiu (Ghost Arrow Feather) - 3 qian
  • Zi Shi Ying (Purple Quartz) - 3 qian
  • Ze Xie (Alisma) - 2 qian
  • Rou Gui (Cinnamon) - 2 qian
  • Yan Hu Suo (Corydalis) - 2 qian
  • Mu Xiang (Wood Fragrance) - 2 qian
  • Da Huang (Rhubarb) - 2 qian, soaked overnight in wine with San Leng, then dried

Additionally:

  • San Leng - 5 qian
  • Bing Lang (Betel Nut) - 2 qian 5 fen
  • Shui Zhi (Leech) - 1 qian, fried until smoke disappears

Take 30 pills with light vinegar soup or warm wine before meals.[65p]

　　肥气丸 【东垣，下同】 　治肝之积，在左胁下如覆杯，有头足，久不愈，令人咳逆痎疟，连年不已，其脉弦而细。　　柴胡二两　黄连七钱　厚朴五钱　炙草三钱　椒炒去汗去目及闭口者，四钱　广朮炮　昆布　人参　皂角去皮弦子煨，各二钱五分　干姜　巴豆去油，各五分　川乌炮去皮脐，一钱二分　白茯苓一钱五分　　右，除茯苓、皂角、巴豆外，为极细末，再另研茯苓、皂角为细末和匀，方旋入巴豆霜和匀，炼蜜丸如桐子大，初服二九，一日加一丸，二日加二丸，渐加至大便微溏；再从两丸加服，周而复始。积减大半，勿服。秋冬加厚朴一半，连前重一两，减黄连一钱半。若治风癎，于一料中加人参、茯苓、菖蒲各三钱，黄连只依春夏用七钱，虽秋冬不减。淡酢汤送下，空心温服。[66p]

Fei Qi Wan (Fat Qi Pill) [Eastern Garden, same below]

This treats the accumulation of the liver, felt under the left rib like a cup, with a head and legs, persisting for a long time without recovery, causing cough, an obstructed feeling, and intermittent fevers that continue for years. The pulse is taut and thin.

Ingredients:

  • Chai Hu (Bupleurum) 2 taels
  • Huang Lian (Coptis) 7 qian
  • Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) 5 qian
  • Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) 3 qian
  • Jiao (Pepper, stir-fried to remove sweat and toxicity, also for closed mouths) 4 qian
  • Guang Xu (Atractylodes) 2.5 qian
  • Kun Bu (Kelp) 2.5 qian
  • Ren Shen (Ginseng) 2.5 qian
  • Zao Jiao (Soapberry, peeled) 2.5 qian
  • Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger) 0.5 qian
  • Ba Dou (Croton) (oiled removed) 0.5 qian
  • Chuan Wu (Radix Aconiti, stir-fried and peeled) 1.2 qian
  • Bai Fu Ling (Poria) 1.5 qian

Preparation:

Excluding Poria, Soapberry, and Ba Dou, grind all to a very fine powder. Separately grind Poria and Soapberry to a fine powder and mix evenly, then incorporate the Ba Dou powder and blend well. Refine with honey into pills the size of catalpa seeds.

Dosage: Start with 2 pills for the first 9 days, increase by 1 pill each day, on the second day increase by 2 pills, gradually increase until the stool is slightly loose; then add 2 pills continuously, repeating this process. Once the accumulation decreases by more than half, do not continue taking. In autumn and winter, increase Hou Po by half, totaling 1.5 taels, and reduce Huang Lian by 1.5 qian.

In case of treating wind convulsions, add Ginseng, Poria, and Shiang Pu (Acorus) 3 qian each to one ingredient, and retain Huang Lian for spring and summer at 7 qian, without reducing for autumn and winter.

Take with light vinegar soup on an empty stomach, consumed warm.[66p]

　　加减肥气丸　春夏合此，治同前。
　　柴胡　厚朴　人参　干姜各五钱　川乌　巴豆霜各三钱　肉桂二钱　黄连一两　川椒　甘草各五分　　右，除巴豆霜外，同为细末，旋入巴豆研匀，炼蜜丸如梧子大，初服二丸，一日加一丸，二日加二丸，渐加至大便微溏，再从二丸加服，淡酢汤下，空心服。秋冬去干姜半钱，加厚朴一倍，减黄连一半。[67p]

Jiajian Feiqi Pill: In spring and summer, use this formula; it is treated the same as before.

Ingredients:

  • Chai Hu (Bupleurum) 5 qian
  • Hou Po (Magnolia Bark) 5 qian
  • Ren Shen (Ginseng) 5 qian
  • Gan Jiang (Dried Ginger) 5 qian
  • Chuan Wu (Lethal Herb) 3 qian
  • Ba Dou Shuang (Physostigma Powder) 3 qian
  • Rou Gui (Cinnamon) 2 qian
  • Huang Lian (Coptis) 1 liang
  • Chuan Jiao (Szechuan Pepper) 5 fen
  • Gan Cao (Licorice) 5 fen

Mix all ingredients into a fine powder except for Ba Dou Shuang, then incorporate the Ba Dou by grinding it together until uniform. Form into pills the size of a walnut. Initially take 2 pills, increasing by 1 pill each day, and on the second day increase by 2 pills, continuing to increase until the stools are slightly loose. Then revert to taking 2 pills. Take with diluted vinegar soup on an empty stomach.

In autumn and winter, reduce Gan Jiang by 0.5 qian, double the Hou Po amount, and halve the Huang Lian amount.[67p]

　　肥气丸 【《三因》】
　　当归头　莪朮各一两半　青皮一两，炒　三棱　铁孕粉与三棱莪朮同入酢煮一复时，各三两　蛇含石火煅酢淬，七钱五分　　右为末，酢煮米糊丸如菉豆大，每服四十丸，用当归浸酒下，食远服。
　　鳖甲丸　治肥气，体瘦无力，少思饮食。　　鳖甲一枚，重四两者，净洗，以酢和黄泥固济，背上可厚三分，令干　大黄炒，二两　荆三棱炮銼　枳壳麸炒微黄，各三两　木香不见火　桃仁汤浸去皮尖双仁者，麸炒微黄细研如膏，各一两五钱　　右除鳖甲外，捣为细末后，泥一风炉子，上开口，可安鳖甲，取前药末，并桃仁膏内鳖甲中，用好米酢二升，时时旋取入鳖甲内，以慢火熬令稠，取出药，却将鳖甲净洗，去泥焙干，捣为细末，与前药同和捣为丸如梧桐子大，每服二十九，空心温酒送下，晚食前再服。[68p]

Fei Qi Pill (from "San Yin")

For the Fei Qi Pill, use:

  • 1.5 taels of Angelica root
  • 1 tael of Atractylodes
  • 1 tael of Green Tangerine peel, stir-fried
  • 3 taels of Triangular Atractylodes
  • 3 taels of Iron Shell Powder, both combined with Triangular Atractylodes and boiled in vinegar for a single session each.

For the ingredients:

  • 7.5 qian of Snake Shell, calcined in vinegar
  • Mix the above into a powder.

Make small pills the size of mung beans using rice paste boiled in vinegar. Take 40 pills per dose, using wine soaked Angelica for ingestion, and take it far from meals.

Tortoise Shell Pill

For treating Fei Qi; suitable for those who are thin and weak, with little appetite and thirst:

  • Use one tortoise shell weighing 4 taels, wash it clean, and mix with vinegar and yellow clay to bind, making it about 1 inch thick on the back; let it dry.

Additionally:

  • 2 taels of prepared Rhubarb
  • 3 taels each of Atractylodes and Myrceugenia, gently roasted to a light yellow
  • 1.5 taels each of Wood Fragrance (not exposed to fire)
  • and Peach Kernels, soaked in broth, skin removed, and finely ground to a paste.

Except for the tortoise shell, crush everything into a fine powder. Take the prepared clay and mold it onto a furnace with an opening, where the tortoise shell can be placed. Use 2 liters of good rice vinegar, infusing occasionally into the tortoise shell with the previous powdered ingredients and peach paste, simmering over low heat until thickened.

Afterward, wash the tortoise shell clean and remove the clay to bake it dry, then crush it into a fine powder and mix it with the previous ingredients, forming pills the size of Wutong seeds. Take 29 pills on an empty stomach, washed down with warm wine, and repeat before dinner.[68p]

　　息贲丸 【东垣，下同】 　治肺之积，在右胁下覆大如杯，久不已，令人洒淅寒热，喘嗽，发肺痈，其脉浮而毛。　　厚朴姜制，八钱　黄连炒，一两三钱　干姜炮　川椒炒去汗　白茯苓另末　紫菀各一钱半　人参二钱　桂枝　桔梗　荆三棱炮　天门冬　陈皮　川乌炮裂，去皮脐　白豆蔻各一钱　青皮五分　巴豆霜四分　　右除茯苓巴豆霜，旋即入外余药，共为细末，炼蜜丸如桐子大，每服二丸。一日加一丸，两日加二丸，加至大便微溏，再从二丸加服。淡姜汤送下，食远服。周而复始。积减大半，勿服。秋冬加厚朴五钱，连前一两三钱；黄连减七钱，用六钱。[69p]

Xibin Pill

It treats accumulation in the lung, located beneath the right rib and as large as a cup. If it lasts for a long time, it leads to chills and fever, coughing, and can develop into pulmonary abscess, with a superficial and wiry pulse.

Ingredients:

  • Thick-skinned bark (processed with ginger) - 8 qian
  • Huanglian (fried) - 1 liang and 3 qian
  • Dried ginger (炮)
  • Chuanjiao (fried to remove sweat)
  • Bai fuling (powdered separately)
  • Ziwan - 1.5 qian each
  • Ginseng - 2 qian
  • Cinnamon twig
  • Platycodon
  • Jinjian (炮)
  • Tianmendong
  • Chenpi
  • Chuanwu (炮 and split, remove skin and navel)
  • Bai doukou - 1 qian
  • Qingpi - 5 fen
  • Baduo shuang - 4 fen

Combine all ingredients, except for bai fuling and baduo shuang, and grind them into a fine powder. Form into pills the size of a tung seed, taking two pills each time.

Increase by one pill daily, and after two days, increase by two pills until the stools are slightly loose. Then revert to taking two pills. Take with bland ginger soup, consuming it far from meals. Repeat this cycle. Once the accumulation is reduced by more than half, do not take further. In autumn and winter, increase thick-skinned bark to 5 qian and maintain the previous amount (1 liang and 3 qian); decrease Huanglian to 6 qian from 7 qian.[69p]

　　加减息贲丸　仲夏合此，其积为病，寒热喘咳，气上奔，脉濇，失精亡血，气滞则短气，血凝泣则寒热相参，气分寒，血分热。治法宜益元气，泄阴火，破气削其坚也。　　川乌　干姜　白豆蔻　桔梗各一钱　紫菀　厚朴　川椒炒去汗　天门冬去心　荆三棱　白茯苓各一钱五分　人参　桂枝各二钱　陈皮八钱　黄连一两三钱　巴豆霜四分　红花少许　青皮七分　　右为末，汤泡蒸饼为丸如桐子大，初服二丸，一日加一丸，二日加二丸，加至大便微溏为度，再从二丸加服，煎生姜汤送下，食前。忌酒湿面腥辣生冷之物。[70p]

Adding and subtracting the "Xi Ben Wan," during midsummer this accumulates as illness, causing chills and fever, shortness of breath and cough, rising qi, a thin pulse, loss of essence and blood, qi stagnation leading to shortness of breath, and blood thickening resulting in alternation of chills and heat, with cold in the qi aspect and heat in the blood aspect. The treatment method should aim to enhance the original energy, drain yin fire, and break up and reduce hardness.

The ingredients are:

  • 1 qian of Chuan Wu
  • 1 qian of Gan Jiang
  • 1 qian of Bai Dou Kou
  • 1 qian of Jie Geng
  • 1 qian and 5 fen of Zi Wan
  • 1 qian and 5 fen of Hou Po
  • 1 qian and 5 fen of Chuan Jiao (fried to remove sweat)
  • 1 qian of Tian Men Dong (heart removed)
  • 1 qian and 5 fen of Jing San Ling
  • 2 qian of Ren Shen
  • 2 qian of Gui Zhi
  • 8 qian of Chen Pi
  • 1 liang and 3 qian of Huang Lian
  • 4 fen of Ba Dou Shuang
  • a little Hong Hua
  • 7 fen of Qing Pi

These should be ground into a powder, soaked in a broth, and formed into pills the size of a tung seed. Initially take 2 pills, increase by 1 pill per day, and after two days increase by 2 pills until the stools are slightly loose. Then return to taking 2 pills, to be taken with decocted ginger soup before meals. Avoid alcohol, damp, fishy, spicy, and cold food items.[70p]

　　息贲汤 【《三因》，下同】
　　半夏汤泡　桂心　人参　葶苈　吴茱萸汤泡　桑白皮炙　炙甘草各一钱五分　　右作一服，水二锺，生姜五片，红枣二枚，煎至一锺，食前服。
　　半夏汤　治肺积息贲咳嗽。
　　细辛去叶苗　半夏制　桔梗炒　桑根白皮炙　前胡各一两五钱　贝母去心　诃黎勒煨去核　柴胡　炙甘草各一两　人参　白朮　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，生姜三片，枣三枚劈破，同煎至七分，去滓温服，食后临卧各一服。[71p]

Xī Bǐn Tāng (Recipe for Relieving Phlegm)

Ingredients:

  • Banxia decoction
  • Gui Xin (Cinnamon), Ren Shen (Ginseng), Ting Li (Radix et Folium Peucedani), Wu Zhu Yu (Evodia) decoction, Sang Bai Pi (Mulberry Bark) roasted, Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) - each 1.5 qian

Preparation:
Mix these ingredients into one dose, add two sheng of water, five slices of ginger, and two red dates. Boil until reduced to one sheng, and consume before meals.

Indication:
Banxia decoction treats phlegm accumulation and alleviates coughing.

Other Ingredients:

  • Xi Xin (Asarum) without leaves and sprouts
  • Banxia (processed)
  • Jie Geng (Platycodon) roasted
  • Sang Gen Bai Pi (Mulberry Root Bark) roasted
  • Qian Hu (Peucedanum) - each 2.5 qian
  • Bei Mu (Fritillaria) without heart
  • He Li Le (Terminalia) stewed without pit
  • Chai Hu (Bupleurum)
  • Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice) - each 1 qian
  • Ren Shen (Ginseng)
  • Bai Zhu (Atractylodes)

Preparation:
Crush these ingredients, take 3 qian per dose, with one bowl of water, three slices of ginger, and three red dates split open, then boil until reduced to seven parts. Strain and take warm, consuming one dose after meals and one before sleeping.[71p]

　　枳实散　治息贲气，腹胁胀硬，咳嗽见血，痰粘不利。　　枳实麸炒　木香　槟榔　赤茯苓　五味子　甜葶苈隔纸炒紫　诃黎勒　甘草微炙，各半两　杏仁一两，汤洗去皮尖双仁，麸炒黄　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一锺，生姜半分，煎至六分，去滓，不拘时温服。
　　伏梁丸 【《三因》，下同】 　治心之积，起脐上，大如臂，上至心下，久不愈，令人烦心，其脉沉而芤。　　茯苓　人参　厚朴姜汁制　枳壳炒　三棱煨　半夏汤泡七次　白朮各等分　　右为末，面糊丸梧子大，每服五十丸，用米饮汤下。
　　干漆丸　治伏梁气，横在心下，坚牢不散，胸中连背多疼。　　干漆炒烟尽　芫花酢炒　鳖甲去裙襕酢炙　硇砂研，各一两　木香　桃仁去皮炒　川乌头去皮脐盐炒，各半两　雄黄细研　麝香研，各二钱半　　右为细末，入别研药令均，酢煮面糊为丸如菉豆大，每服十丸，食前温酒送下。[72p]

Zhi Shi San: Treats hiccuping and rebellious qi, abdominal and flank distension and hardness, coughing with blood, and sticky phlegm that is not easy to expel.

Ingredients: Zhi Shi (bitter orange) stir-fried with bran, Mu Xiang (costus), Bing Lang (betel nut), Chi Fu Ling (red poria), Wu Wei Zi (schisandra), Tian Ting Li (sweet-leafed herb) stir-fried with purple paper, He Li Luo (black pepper), and Gan Cao (licorice) lightly roasted, each in equal parts; Xing Ren (apricot kernel) one liang, soaked in water and peeled, then double-kerneled, stir-fried until yellow.

Dosage: Grind and take three qian each time, with one zhong (measuring cup) of water and half a fen of ginger, decoct until six parts remain, then strain and take warm at any time.

Fu Liang Wan: Treats accumulation in the heart, located above the navel, as large as an arm, reaching below the heart, not healing for a long time, causing distress with deep and weak pulses.

Ingredients: Fu Ling (poria), Ren Shen (ginseng), Hou Po (magnolia bark) with ginger juice, Zhi Ke (bitter orange) stir-fried, San Leng (sparganii rhizome) prepared with water, and Ban Xia (pinellia) soaked in soup seven times, Bai Zhu (atractylodes), each in equal parts.

Dosage: Grind into a fine powder and make into pills the size of a walnut, taking fifty pills each time, swallowed with rice wine.

Gan Qi Wan: Treats lurking qi, horizontally lodged below the heart, hard and fixed, with chest and back pain.

Ingredients: Gan Qi (lacquer tree) stir-fried until smoke is gone, Yan Hua (milkweed) vinegar stir-fried, Gui Jia (soft-shelled turtle shell) cleaned and vinegar roasted, Nao Sha (arsenic) ground, each one liang; Mu Xiang, Tao Ren (peach kernel) peeled and stir-fried, Chuan Wu Tou (chuan woad) peeled and salted stir-fried, each half a liang; Xiong Huang (realgar) finely ground and She Xiang (musk) ground, each two qian and half.

Dosage: Grind into a fine powder, mix with other ground herbs to make a uniform paste, then vinegar-cooked into small pills the size of mung beans. Take ten pills each time with warm wine before meals.[72p]

　　半夏散　治伏梁积，心下硬急，满闷不能食，胸背疼痛。　　半夏制　鳖甲酢炙，各一两半　桂心　大黄炒　诃黎勒皮　前胡　当归焙　青橘皮　槟榔　木香　荆三棱炮，各一两　　右为末，每服三钱，水一锺，生姜半分，煎至六分，去滓，不拘时稍热服。
　　痞气丸 【东垣，下同】 　治脾之积在胃脘，覆大如盘，久不愈，令人四肢不收，发黄疸，饮食不为肌肤，其脉大而长。　　厚朴姜制，半两　黄连八钱　吴茱萸洗，三钱　黄芩　白朮各二钱　茵陈酒炙炒　缩砂仁　干姜炮，各一钱五分　白茯苓另为末　人参　泽泻各一钱　川乌炮去皮脐　川椒各五分　巴豆霜另研　桂各四分　　右除茯苓、巴豆霜，另研为末，旋入外余药，同为细末，炼蜜丸桐子大，初服二丸，一日加一丸，二日加二丸，渐加至大便微溏，再从二丸加服，淡甘草汤下，食远服。周而复始。积减大半，勿服。[73p]

Ban Xia San: Treats phlegm accumulation beneath the diaphragm, causing a hard and urgent sensation in the heart, fullness and inability to eat, and pain in the chest and back. Ingredients include Ban Xia, Zhi Bie Jia, vinegar and roasted, each one tael; Gui Xin, Da Huang (stir-fried), He Li Le Pi, Qian Hu, Dang Gui (roasted), Qing Ju Pi, Bing Lang, Mu Xiang, and Jing San Ling (cooked), each one tael. Pi Qi Wan [Dong Yuan, same below]: Treats spleen accumulation in the epigastric region, which feels as large as a plate, not healing for a long time, causing weakness in the limbs, yellow jaundice, and inability to nourish the muscles from food, with a large and long pulse. Ingredients include Hou Po and Jiang Zhi, half a tael; Huang Lian, eight qian; Wu Zhu Yu, washed, three qian; Huang Qin and Bai Zhu, each two qian; Yin Chen (wine roasted), Suo Sha Ren, and Gan Jiang (cooked), each one and a half qian; Bai Fu Ling, ground separately; Ren Shen and Ze Xie, each one qian; Chuan Wu (cooked, skin and navel removed) and Chuan Jiao, each half a qian; Ba Dou Shuang, ground separately; Gui, each four fen. Except for Bai Fu Ling and Ba Dou Shuang, grind the remaining ingredients into a fine powder, mix in with the others, and form into honey pills the size of tung seeds. Initially take two pills, increase by one pill each day, two pills every second day, gradually increasing until the stool is slightly loose, then reduce back to two pills, taken with a mild licorice decoction, away from meals. Repeat this cycle. If the accumulation reduces significantly, do not continue taking.[73p]

　　蒜红丸 【《三因》，下同】 　治脾积腹胀如鼓，青筋浮起，坐卧不得者。　　丁香　木香　沉香　缩砂仁　青皮　槟榔　橘红　蓬莪朮　草果去皮　牵牛各一两　粉霜　肉豆蔻面裹煨，各一钱　白茯苓　人参各半两　蒜二百瓣，半用生，半火煨熟　　右为细末，以生熟蒜研膏，生绢绞取汁，和药为丸如梧子大，每服五七丸，加至十五丸，食后淡盐汤送下，忌咸酸鱼鲊茶酱腌藏鸡鸭生冷马牛杂肉之类，只可食淡白粥百日。

Yunqi Decoction: Used for treating accumulation of phlegm in the spleen, discomfort in the stomach, thinness, and loss of appetite.

　　奔豚丸 【东垣】 　治肾之积，发于小腹，上至心下，若豚状，或上或下，无时，久不已，令人喘逆，骨痿少气，及治男子内结七疝，女子瘕聚带下，其脉沉而滑。　　厚朴姜制，七钱　黄连炒，五钱　楝子酒煮，三钱　白茯苓另末　泽泻　菖蒲各二钱　附子去皮　全蝎　独活各一钱　延胡索一钱半　川乌炮　丁香各五分　巴豆霜四分　肉桂二分　　右除巴豆霜茯苓另为末，旋入外余药为细末，炼蜜丸如梧子大，初服二丸，一日加一丸，二日加二丸，渐加至大便微溏，再从二丸加服，淡盐汤下，食远服。周而复始，积减大半，勿服。秋冬加厚朴半两，连前一两二钱。如积势坚大，先服前药，不减，于一料中加存性牡蛎三钱，疝带下勿加。如积满腹或半腹，先治其所起是何积，当先服本脏积药，诸积疾自愈，是治其本也。余积皆然。如觉热加黄连，气短减厚朴，闷乱减桂。[77p]

Bentan Pill (from Dongyuan)

This formula treats the accumulation in the kidneys that manifests in the lower abdomen and rises to the heart, resembling a blubbering piglet. It may rise or fall without a specific time frame, persists for a long time, and causes breathlessness, weakness in the bones, and shortness of breath. It also treats men's internal issues related to the seven types of hernias and women's masses with abnormal discharges. The pulse is deep and slippery.

  • Magnolia Bark (processed with ginger), 7 qian
  • Fried Coptis, 5 qian
  • Ailanthus (boiled in wine), 3 qian
  • White Poria (ground separately)
  • Alisma, Sweet Flag, each 2 qian
  • Prepared Aconite (peeled), Scorpion, and Notopterygium, each 1 qian
  • Yanhusuo, 1.5 qian
  • Chuanwu (fried) and Clove, each 5 fen
  • Cowherb powder, 4 fen
  • Cinnamon, 2 fen

Grind the Poria and Cowherb separately into powder, then mix the remaining herbs into a fine powder. Roll the mixture into pills the size of a jujube. Initially, take 2 pills, add one pill each day, and increase by two pills every two days until the stool becomes slightly loose. After that, reduce back to 2 pills, taking them with light salted soup and having meals spaced apart.

Repeat this cycle until the accumulation decreases by more than half, and avoid further intake. In autumn and winter, increase the Magnolia Bark by half a tael, keeping the previous amount at 1 tael and 2 qian. If the accumulation is firm and large, take the prior medicine first without reducing it, and in this formulation, add 3 qian of preserved oyster, but do not add if there is hernia or abnormal discharge.

If the abdomen is full or half full, first address the source of the accumulation. The foundational medication should be taken to relieve any type of accumulation diseases for natural recovery. The same applies to all accumulations. If there is a sensation of heat, add Coptis; if short of breath, reduce Magnolia Bark; and if there is heaviness and chaos, reduce Cinnamon.[77p]

Bēntún Táng (Bēntún Decoction)

Wan Bing Zi Wan
[From "Yuan Rong"]
For treating persistent abdominal ailments resembling a large lump.

Wen Bai Wan
[From "He Ji"]
For treating accumulation in the heart and abdomen, chronic lumps the size of large cups; jaundice and retained food; morning vomiting; fullness and breathlessness; regular abdominal distension; hardness beneath the heart, causing palpitations; lateral pain in the sides; ten kinds of water retention; eight types of blockage; reversed stomach qi resulting in vomiting; food choking; five types of dysuria; nine types of heart pain; chronic indigestion from accumulated food; or persistent malaria.
Use the basic formula of Wan Bing Zi Wan, reducing Qiang Huo, Du Huo, and Fang Feng. For lung issues with phlegm, add Ren Shen and Ziwan; for heart distress, add Jiangju, Huang Lian, and Tao Ren; for spleen qi stagnation, add Wu Zhu Yu and dried ginger; for liver Qi issues, add Chai Hu and Chuan Xiong; for kidney issues, add Ding Xiang, Fu Ling, and Yuan Zhi.[79p]

　　万病感应丸
　　即前温白丸内，加羌活、三棱、甘遂、杏仁、防风各一两五钱，威灵仙一两，减蜀椒。
　　千金硝石丸　止可磨块，不令困人，须量虚实。　　硝石六两　大黄八两　人参　甘草各三两　　右为细末，以三年苦酒三升置器中，以竹片作刻记，每人一升作一刻，先入大黄，不住手搅，使微沸，尽一刻，乃下余药，又尽一刻微火熬，便可丸如鸡子黄大，每服一丸。如不用大丸，作梧子大，每服三十丸。服后下如鸡肝米泔赤黑色等物。下后，忌风冷，宜软粥将息。[80p]

Ten-Thousand Sickness Response Pill

This is made by adding Qiankang, Sanling, Gansui, Apricot Kernels, and Fangfeng, each 1.5 taels, to the original Wenbai Pill, along with 1 tael of Weilingxian and a reduced amount of Sichuan Pepper.

Thousand Gold Nitre Pill

This should be ground into blocks, avoiding causing distress; careful measurement of deficiency and excess is required.

Six taels of Nitre, eight taels of Da Huang, and three taels each of Ginseng and Licorice are used.

The above are to be ground into a fine powder, then placed in a container with three sheng of three-year-old bitter wine. Use a bamboo stick to mark increments; each person receives one sheng for one mark.

First, add Da Huang while continually stirring until it lightly boils; finish one mark, then add the remaining medicines and finish another mark, simmering over a gentle flame. Form the mixture into pills the size of egg yolks, taking one pill each time.

If larger pills are not used, make them the size of a nut, taking thirty pills per dose.

After taking, expect to expel substances resembling dark red and black matter similar to chicken liver rice gruel. Following the expulsion, avoid cold wind and rest with soft porridge.[80p]

　　酢煮三棱丸 【《宝鉴》，下同】 　治一切积聚，不拘年深日久，治之神效。　　荆三棱四两，酢煮竹刀切晒　川芎二两，酢煮切　大黄半两，酢浸湿纸裹煨过切　　右为末，酢糊丸如桐子大，每服三十丸，温水下，无时。病甚者一月效，小者半月效。
　　圣散子　治远年积块，及妇人干血气。　　硇砂　大黄各八钱　麦糵炒取净面，六两　干漆炒烟尽，三两　萹蓄　茴香炒　槟榔各一两　　妇人干血气加穿山甲二两炮。右为细末，每服五钱，临卧温酒调下，仰卧，此药只在心头，至天明大便如烂鱼肠，小便赤为验。药并无毒，有神效。小儿用一钱，十五以上三钱，空心服之更效。此按古本校定，今《纲目》刻本，硇砂乃六两，大黄乃八两，岂不悞人！[81p]

Boiled Acetic Three-Angled Round
Treats all accumulations, regardless of duration; its effect is miraculous.

  • Three liang of three-angled herb, boiled in vinegar, cut and dried.
  • Two liang of chuanxiong, boiled in vinegar and cut.
  • Half a liang of rhubarb, soaked in vinegar, wrapped in damp paper, steamed, and cut.
    Grind the above into a powder, mix with vinegar to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take thirty pills at a time with warm water, at any time. For severe cases, effects in one month; for milder cases, effects in half a month.

Holy Powder
Treats long-standing masses and women's blood conditions.

  • Eight qian each of realgar and rhubarb.
  • Six liang of fried wheat bran, cleaned.
  • Three liang of fried lacquer until the smoke disappears.
  • One liang each of alisma and fennel, fried.
  • One liang of areca nut.
    For women's blood conditions, add two liang of pangolin, cooked. Grind finely. Take five qian before bed, mixed with warm wine, lying on your back. This medicine affects only the heart; by dawn, expect a bowel movement resembling rotten fish guts, and red urine as verification. This medicine is non-toxic and highly effective. For children, take one qian; for those over fifteen, three qian; taking it on an empty stomach is more effective. This conforms to the ancient text; the current "Gāngmù" printed edition incorrectly lists realgar as six liang and rhubarb as eight liang, which misleads people![81p]

　　鸡爪三棱丸　治五脏痃癖气块。
　　鸡爪三棱　石三棱　荆三棱　木香　青皮　陈皮去白，各半两　硇砂三钱　槟榔一两　肉豆蔻一两　　右为细末，生姜汁打面糊为丸桐子大，每服二十丸，姜汤下，空心临卧各一服。忌一切生冷硬粘物。
　　硇砂煎丸　消磨积块痃癖，一切凝滞。　　黑附子二枚，各重五饯以上，正坐妥者，炮裂去皮脐剜作瓮子　硇砂　木香各三钱　川荜茇　破故纸隔纸微炒，各一两　　右将硇砂末，用一盏水续续化开，纳在瓮内，火上熬干为末，安在附子瓮内，却用剜出附子末填盖，口用和成白面裹，约半指厚，慢灰火内烧匀，黄色，去面，同木香等为细末，却用元裹附子熟黄面为末，酢调煮糊为丸如桐子，每服十五丸至三十丸，生姜汤下。[82p]

Chicken Claw Sanling Pill treats internal blockages and swelling in the five organs.

Ingredients:
Chicken Claw Sanling, Shisanling, Jing Sanling, Mu Xiang, Qing Pi, Chen Pi (white part removed), each half a tael; Nüsha (realgar) three qian; Betel nut one tael; Nutmeg one tael.

Grind these into a fine powder, mix with fresh ginger juice to form pills the size of tung seeds. Take twenty pills with ginger soup on an empty stomach before lying down. Avoid all raw, cold, hard, and sticky foods.

Nüsha-infused pills eliminate accumulated masses and stasis.

For preparation: Take two pieces of black Aconite, each weighing five jiao or more. Properly seated, roast them until cracked, then remove the skin and navel, creating a jar. Add three qian of Nüsha and Mu Xiang, and one tael each of Sichuan Pepper and broken aged paper, slightly roasted under parchment.

Dissolve the Nüsha powder in one cup of water and put it in the jar, then simmer until dry, turning it into a powder. Fill the Aconite jar with this powder, then cover it with Aconite powder. The mouth should be wrapped with a mixture of white flour to a thickness of about half a finger, slowly bake over ash until evenly yellow, then remove the flour. Grind this with Mu Xiang and the rest into a fine powder.

Finally, make pills the size of tung seeds by mixing with vinegar and cooking to form a paste. Take fifteen to thirty pills with ginger soup.[82p]

　　削坚丸　治五积六聚，气结成块，食积癖瘕，心腹胀满，瘦瘁少食。　　鳖甲酢浸两宿，去裙襕，再蘸酢炙黄，取末称　干漆捣碎，炒令烟出，取末称　荆三棱銼如半枣大，好酢浸两宿焙，取末称，各二两半　肉桂去粗皮　细松烟墨烧去胶　沉香　干姜炮　没药另研　萝卜子　干蝎去毒炒　胡椒　槟榔　木香　硇砂通明者为末，另研飞，各五钱　乳香另研　粉霜另研　轻粉各二钱五分　　右为细末研匀，好酢煮薄面糊为丸如小菉豆大，每服二十丸，淡酢煎生姜汤送下，日进二服，夜间服。如未利，渐加丸数服，微利即减。
　　一肾散　消积块，进饮食。
　　橘红一斤　甘草四两　盐五钱
　　右用水十碗，从早煮至夜，以烂为度，水干则添水，晒干为末，淡姜汤调下。有块者，加姜黄半两，同前药煮。气滞，加香附二两，同前药煮。气虚者，加沉香半两，另入。噤口痢，加莲肉二两，去心另入。[83p]

Xiao Jian Wan treats accumulation of the five and six internal excesses, qi stagnation forming lumps, food accumulation resulting in abdominal distension, and emaciation due to inadequate appetite.

To prepare, soak turtle shell in vinegar for two nights, remove the skirt, and dip in vinegar again then roast until yellow; grind into powder as measured. Crush the lacquer and stir-fry until it smokes; grind into powder as measured. Grind the three-edged needle to about the size of half a jujube, soak in vinegar for two nights and roast, then grind into powder as measured. Use two and a half taels each of cinnamon (removing the coarse skin), fine soot from pine smoke (remove the glue), agarwood, dried ginger (roasted), myrrh (ground separately), radish seeds, dried scorpion (de-toxified and stir-fried), pepper, areca nut, and wood fragrance. Use five qian each of transparent natron, ground separately. Also, grind frankincense and talcum powder separately. Use two qian and five fen each of light powder.

Mix these finely ground powders well. Use vinegar to boil a thin paste and form pills about the size of small soybeans. Take twenty pills each time, taking them down with a decoction of fresh ginger in light vinegar. Take two doses daily; if no results, gradually increase the number of pills; if there’s slight efficacy, reduce the intake.

Yi Shen San dispels accumulations and helps with food intake.

For this, use one jin of dried tangerine peel, four taels of licorice, and five qian of salt.

Boil them with ten bowls of water from morning until night until they are soft; if the water dries up, add more. Dry and grind to powder, and take with light ginger decoction. For lumps, add half a tael of turmeric and cook with the previous herbs. For qi stagnation, add two taels of cyperus and cook with the previous herbs. For qi deficiency, add half a tael of agarwood and add separately. For dysentery with a closed mouth, add two taels of lotus seeds (removing the hearts) and add separately.[83p]

　　阿魏丸　去诸积。

Sanju Decoction [from "Three Causes"]:

  • Treats the accumulation of the nine gas types, presenting as masses like zhengjia; symptoms include rising and falling with gas, sharp pain in the heart and abdomen, stabbing pain in the lower ribs, abdominal distention (monthly true), and difficulty with urination and defecation.
  • Banxia decocted and soaked seven times; each seven qian and five fen of angelica, betel nut; two taels each of skinless bitter almond (stir-fried), dried tangerine peel (white removed), honey-fried licorice, cassia bark, poria; each one tael of stir-fried bitter orange peel, prepared aconite (peeled and pricked), chuanxiong, and thick bark ginger; and wu zhu yu soaked in decoction. Each dose is four qian in water, three slices of ginger, and decocted until reduced to seven parts, taken warm before meals. If there is difficulty in defecation, add rhubarb.[84p]

Newly Formulated Yin-Yang Accumulation Pills
[From "Essential Reads in Medicine"]
Treats the five accumulations and six gatherings, seven symptoms and eight masses, lumps and abscesses, parasitic blood, phlegm and food, effective regardless of yin or yang.
Ingredients:

  • 1 liang of Wu Yao (Evodia)
  • 1 liang of roasted dried ginger
  • 1 liang of peeled cinnamon bark
  • 1 liang of roasted Chuan Wu (Aconite)
  • 1 liang of roasted Huang Lian (Coptis)
  • 1 liang of washed Ban Xia (Pinellia)
  • 1 liang of Chen Pi (tangerine peel)
  • 1 liang of Fu Ling (Poria)
  • 1 liang of Bian Dou (Job's tears)
  • 1 liang of Xiang Fu (sandalwood)
  • 1 liang of roasted Hou Po (magnolia bark)
  • 1 liang of roasted Zhi Shi (bitter orange)
  • 8 qian of Chao Shu (Acorus) (avoid using iron in preparation)
  • 8 qian of Yan Hu Suo (Corydalis)
  • 8 qian of Ren Shen (ginseng)
  • 8 qian of powdered amber
  • 8 qian of Jie Geng (balloon flower)
  • 5 qian of Ba Shuang (bitter almond)

Grind all ingredients into a fine powder, add 6 liang of soap shavings, boil in liquid until it forms pills the size of mung beans. Take 8 fen at a time, gradually increasing by 1.5 fen, with ginger soup for ingestion.

Aweigh Ointment: Treats all types of masses; additionally take Hu Huang Lian pills.

Ingredients: Qiang Huo, Du Huo, Yuan Shen, Guan Gui, Chi Shao Yao, Chuan Shan Jia (pangolin), Sheng Di Huang, Liang Tou Jian, Da Huang, Bai Zhi, Tian Ma – each five qian; Huai Zhi, Liu Zhi, Tao Zhi – each three qian; twenty seeds of Mu Bie Zi; a clump of hair the size of a chicken egg; Hong Hua four qian.

Preparation: Use two jin and four liang of fragrant oil, fry until black and remove the dregs, mix in hair and further fry, then remove dregs again. Gradually add Huang Dan decoction, adjusting to the right consistency. Incorporate Mang Xiao, Aweigh, Su He oil, Ru Xiang, and Mo Yao – each five qian; Mix in three qian of She Xiang until uniformly combined to form ointment for application to the affected area. For internal pills, ensure genuine Huang Dan is used.

When applying the ointment, first use (stone sulfate) nitrate, uniformly spread half a finger thick over the affected area, cover with paper, and use a hot iron to press for a long time. If the nitrate depletes, add more and continue pressing for about two hours before applying the ointment. If there is liver accumulation, add powdered aloe to the pressing mixture.

Hu Qi Decoction (from "San Yin"): Treats stagnant breath.

Baillou Pill from Hejian treats all forms of labor-induced diseases caused by stagnation. For those who do not respond to medication or have complications, it is advisable to take this remedy.

Ingredients:

  • 1 qian of fried Angelica
  • 1 qian of powdered frankincense
  • 1 qian of powdered myrrh
  • 2 qian of ginseng
  • 14 pieces of wingless and legless cicada
  • Fried leech
  • 14 peach seeds, without skin and tip
  • 4 qian of rhubarb

Grind the above into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of tung seeds. This makes about 100 pills. Take with Baillou water at dawn and consume congee for ten days. Baillou water is made by stirring water a hundred times; this is Zhuang Jing's sweet and mellow water.

Tongyuan Erba Dan treats accumulations.

Ingredients:

  • 8 liang of Coptis
  • 5 qian each of peony, angelica, raw rhubarb, and black plum

Grind the ingredients into powder, take the belly of a male pig, place the medicine inside, sew it up, and spread 2 jin of leeks in a pot. Steam for one day until the medicine is well-cooked. Take out and crush into pills the size of walnuts, taking 70 pills with ginger soup on an empty stomach. If needed, evacuate once or twice, and supplement with congee.

Xiangling Pill treats five accumulations and six masses.

　　大七气汤　治五积六聚，心腹痛胀，二便不利。　　三棱　蓬朮　青皮　陈皮　桔梗　藿香　益智仁　香附子　肉桂　甘草各一钱　　右銼，作一贴，姜三片，枣二枚，水煎服。一方加大黄、槟榔各一钱，治诸痞积面色萎黄，四肢无力，皆缘内有虫积，或好食生米，或壁土，或茶炭咸辣等物，只此一服除根。用水煎露一宿，空心温服，不得些少饮食，不然，则药力减而虫积不行矣。服后，心腹痛，当下恶物，如鱼冻虫鳖，至日午下积尽，方用温粥止之。
　　溃坚汤 【《回春》，下同】 　治五积六聚，诸般痞块。　　当归　白朮　半夏　陈皮　枳实　山楂肉　香附　厚朴　缩砂各一钱　木香五分，磨汁　　右銼，作一贴，水煎调木香汁服之。一方，加海粉、瓦垄子、鳖甲炙为未，将阿魏酢煮化，入姜汁糊和丸梧子大，酒下五七十丸。名溃坚丸。[88p]

Da Qi Decoction treats the five accumulations and six gatherings, as well as pain and distension in the heart and abdomen, and difficulty in urination. Ingredients: 3 grams each of Sanling, Ganshu, Qingpi, Chenpi, Jiegeng, Huoxiang, Yizhiren, Xiangfuzi, Rougui, and Gancao. Chop these up, make into a dose, and add three slices of ginger and two jujubes. Boil in water and take it as a decoction. There is also a recipe that adds 3 grams each of Dahuang and Binglang, which treats various conditions of distension and a sallow complexion with weakness in the limbs, often due to internal accumulation of parasites that prefer raw rice, wall soil, or salty-spicy substances. This remedy eliminates the root cause. Boil in water, let it steep overnight, and take it on an empty stomach warm. Avoid any food or drink, otherwise, the efficacy will be diminished and the parasite accumulation will not be resolved. After taking it, if there is pain in the heart and abdomen, the expelled substance will be things like fish, worms, or turtles, and only when everything is expelled by noon should one begin to consume warm porridge to stop further discomfort.

Kui Jian Decoction treats the five accumulations and six gatherings, and various kinds of lumps. Ingredients: 3 grams each of Danggui, Baizhu, Banxia, Chenpi, Zhishi, Shan Zha meat, Xiangfu, Houpu, and Suoshan, with 2.5 grams of Muxiang juice prepared by grinding. Chop these up, make into a dose, and prepare with water and the wood fragrant juice for consumption. Another recipe includes Hai Fen, Wa Longzi, and fried Bie Jia, and for the agent, fry Asafoetida until it melts and mix with ginger juice to form pills the size of a walnut, to be taken with wine, about 50 to 70 pills. This is called Kui Jian Pills.[88p]

Real Person's Iron Soup treats the five accumulations and six gatherings, and issues like abscesses and masses. The ingredients are: three grams each of Sanleng, Poria, Qingpi, Chenpi, Hawthorn flesh, Shenqu, Zhishi, Houpo, Huanglian, Danggui, Xiangfuzi, Chuanxiong, Taoren, and Binglang; three grams each of Honghua, Muxiang, and Gancao. Grind these together into a paste, add three slices of ginger and one date, then decoct and consume.

Quartz Powder [from "Three Causes"] treats stone masses. The ingredients are: one tael of purple quartz, five qian each of Dangguiwei, Verbena, and stir-fried Honghua, five qian of dried plum flesh; three qian each of vinegar-fried Poria, vinegar-fried Sanleng, and Su Mu; one qian each of Myrrh, Amber, and Gancao. Grind these into a powder and mix with two qian of strong decocted Su Mu wine. If avoiding alcohol, use ginger soup.

Red Pills [from "Effective Treatment"] treat food accumulation, wine accumulation, spleen accumulation, and various blood and energy-related masses. The ingredients are: five liang each of Sanleng, Poria, Qingpi, and Chenpi; one liang each of pepper and dried ginger. Grind into a powder, vinegar-cook into a paste, roll into pills the size of a nut, coat with red alum, and swallow five to seventy pills with ginger soup.

Spleen Assisting Pills [from Danxi] treat food accumulation. The ingredients are: three liang of Hawthorn flesh, five qian each of Lianqiao, Chenpi, and stir-fried Radish seeds; one qian each of red Poria and Banxia. Grind these into a powder, form into pills the size of a mung bean, and swallow five to seventy pills with warm water.[89p]

Miao Ying Dan
Treats insect and poison from food and drink, or when one consumes fruits, vegetables, seeds, and eggs, leading to the formation of worms, snakes, fish, and soft-shelled turtles in the stomach, or retained food causing lumps.
Four pieces of prepared aconite, each weighing seven qian, remove the skin and navel to form a jar, mix with one and a half liang of realgar, wrap in flour, and steam until cooked, discarding the flour. Add three liang and five qian each of: pepper, wood incense, orange peel, and ruptured old paper.
Grind these into a powder, mix with flour to form pills the size of a jujube, and take thirty pills with ginger and tangerine peel decoction.

Gui Xiang Wan
Treats accumulation due to excessive consumption of a variety of melons and fruits, causing abdominal distension and urgent gas.
One liang of cassia bark, one qian of musk.
Grind into a powder, form rice-sized pills, and swallow fifteen pills with clear broth.

Sheng Hong Wan
Treats blood accumulation from alcohol and the accumulation of spleen blood and gas in women.
One liang each of: san leng, hao ju, stir-fried in vinegar; 青皮 (qing pi); chen pi; stir-fried dried ginger; and stir-fried liang jiang. Two liang of xiang fu zi, also stir-fried in vinegar.
Grind these into a powder, mix with vinegar to form pills the size of a jujube, and take thirty to fifty pills with ginger decoction.

Zeng Wei Si Wu Tang
Treats blood accumulation.
Equal parts of: cooked rehmannia, angelica sinensis, chuanxiong, white peony root, san leng, hao ju, stir-fried dry lacquer, and cinnamon.
Make a decoction with water and consume.[90p]

San Leng Jian: This remedy treats food-related ailments, alcohol addiction, blood clots, and qi blockages. Combine four taels each of San Leng (three-angled herb) and Peng Zhu (corydalis), and one tael of Yuan Hua (peony flower) in a ceramic container. Soak with five cups of rice vinegar, seal the container, and heat over charcoal until dry. Remove the herbs, and slightly char the Yuan Hua with leftover vinegar, then dry it completely. Grind the mixture to a fine powder, mix with vinegar to form pills the size of black beans, and take fifteen pills with ginger tea.

Qian Jin Hua Qi Wan: This remedy treats abdominal gas and bloating in men. Ingredients include one tael each of Hou Po (magnolia bark), Fu Ping (pericarpium), Bai Shao (white peony), Chuan Xiong (ligusticum), Bai Zhi (angelica), Yin Pi (cortex), Chen Pi (aged tangerine peel), Zhi Ke (bitter orange), Xiang Fu (cyperus), Sha Ren (amomum fruit), Bai Dou Kou (white cardamom), San Leng, E Zhu (curcuma), and Yan Hu (dipsacus), one tael each of Huo Xiang (patchouli), Ban Xia (pinellia), Cao Guo (grass fruit), and Bing Lang (betel nut), each one and a half taels; five qian each of Xiao Hui Xiang (fennel), Gan Jiang (dried ginger), and Mu Xiang (saussurea); and three qian of Gan Cao (licorice) and two qian of Ding Xiang (clove). Grind the ingredients into a powder, add three slices of raw ginger, decoct in water, and take the warm liquid on an empty stomach.

Jin Lu Wan: This remedy treats all types of accumulations and pain in the abdomen. Ingredients include one tael each of Cao Wu (aconite), Huang Lian (coptis), Sheng Di Huang (fresh rehmannia), Bei Mu (fritillaria), Jie Geng (balloon flower), Bai Dou (physostegia), Chai Hu (bupleurum), Zi Wan (aster), Wu Zhu Yu (evodia), Chang Pu (acetosella), Gan Jiang, Bai Fu Ling (poria), Gui Xin (cinnamon heart), Chuan Xiong, Ren Shen (ginseng), Gan Cao, Fang Feng (siler), Hou Po, Zhi Ke, and Bie Jia (tortoise shell), each five qian. Grind into a fine powder, mix with water to form pills the size of a jujube, and take three to five pills with ginger tea.[91p]

　　秘方化滞丸 【丹溪】 　理一切气，化一切积，久坚沉痼，磨之自消，暴积乍留，导之立去。夺造化，有通塞之功；调阴阳，有补泻之妙。　　三棱　蓬朮并煨，各四钱八分　半夏曲　木香　丁香　青皮　陈皮并去白　黄连各二钱五分　巴豆肉酢浸一宿熬干，六钱　乌梅肉焙末，五钱　　右为末，以乌梅末入白面少许煮作糊，和丸黍米大，每服五七丸至十丸。欲通利则以热汤下，欲磨积则以陈皮汤下，欲止泄则饮冷水。[92p]

Jingpeng Jianwan (Pill of Orchid and Poppy)

This pill eliminates illnesses caused by cold and heat accumulation, breaking phlegm lumps and digesting stagnant food.

  • Mix equal parts of Sanleng, Pengzhu, and soak in wine for three days. In summer, soak for one day, then take out and fry together with thirty-eight grains of Ba Dou until yellow. Remove the Ba Dou, soak in broth, and discard the white parts, using two taels each of
  • Wood Incense, Zhiqiao, Qingpi, and Fried Fennel.
  • Prepare one tael each of Betel Nut.

Grind the above ingredients into a powder, mix with flour to form pills the size of mung beans, and take three to fifty pills with ginger soup.

Mifa Huati Wan (Secret Formula for Dispelling Stagnation Pill)

This pill regulates all qi, transforms all accumulations, and can resolve long-standing and stubborn ailments; it dissolves by grinding. Instant accumulations will be easily expelled. It seizes vitality, functioning to open blockages; it balances yin and yang, possessing the nuances of nourishment and drainage.

  • Combine Sanleng and Pengzhu, each four qian and eight fen.
  • Add Banxia Qu, Wood Incense, Cloves, Qingpi, Chenpi (discarding the white), and Huanglian, each two qian and five fen.
  • Soak Ba Dou meat overnight in vinegar and then boil to dryness, six qian.
  • Powder Wu Mei meat, five qian.

Grind into a powder, then take a small amount of Wu Mei powder and mix with a little white flour to make a paste, forming pills the size of millet. Take five to ten pills each time. For promoting flow, take with hot soup; for grinding accumulations, take with Chenpi soup; to stop diarrhea, drink cold water.[92p]

Yannian Huming Dan: Treats thirty-six types of accumulations, twenty-four types of qi disorders, and blood clots caused by parasites.

Ingredients include:

  • Ten ounces of rhubarb, half raw and half soaked in vinegar, sliced and dried
  • Frankincense, myrrh, and light powder, each one qian
  • Yuanhua and tortoise shell (vinegar-baked), each five qian
  • Qianghuo and Notopterygium pulverized
  • One liang of black lump powder
  • Two and a half qian of aged tangerine peel, soaked overnight with Yuanhua, then dried

The above ingredients are ground into powder, mixed with honey and pounded a thousand times. Each liang produces four pills, which should be thoroughly chewed and taken with warm water, prior to sleep, to expel harmful substances by morning. For three days, consume only plain congee to rest and avoid cold and greasy foods.[94p]

Amber Paste (Danxi): Apply to accumulative masses.

  • Rhubarb (1 tael)
  • Saltpeter (1 tael)

Five Immortal Paste (Hui Chun): Treats all forms of lumps and accumulative conditions.

  • Rhubarb
  • Soap beans
  • Fresh ginger
  • Fresh scallions
  • Garlic (each 0.5 kg)

Mince together, boil with water to extract juice, then strain and boil until it thickens into a paste, achieving a black color. Spread it on silk, prick the affected area with a needle, and then apply the paste.

Paste for Lumps (Entering the Door):

  • Water red flower seeds (2 qian)
  • Fresh rhubarb
  • Saltpeter
  • Gardenia fruit
  • Lime (each 1 qian)
  • A block of sake yeast (about the size of an egg)

Mince the above into a paste, spread on cloth, and apply to the lump, then use a hot water bottle to press a handkerchief onto it. After three days, remove it; the flesh will be as black as ink, which indicates its effectiveness.[95p]

　　保安丸　治症积，心腹内结如拳，渐上不止，抢心疼痛，及绕脐腹痛不可忍者。　　大黄三两，蒸熟切片焙　大附子五钱，去脐皮　干姜一两，炮　鳖甲一两半，酢煮一复时，炙黄炒　　右为末，取三年米酢一大升，先煮四五合，然后和药丸如桐子大，每服十丸至二十丸，空心酢或酒米饮下后取积如鱼肠脓血烂肉汁清泥，当下。
　　小七香丸 【《和剂》，下同】 　温中快膈，化积和气。治中酒呕逆，气膈食噎，茶酒食积。　　甘松八两　益智仁六两　香附子炒　丁香皮　甘草炙，各十二两　蓬朮煨　缩砂各二两　　右为末，蒸饼为丸菉豆大，每服二十丸。温酒姜汤热水任下。

Bao An Pill: Treats symptoms of accumulation; when the abdomen feels like a clenched fist, gradually worsening, causing sharp heart pain and intolerable pain around the navel and abdomen.

Ingredients:

  • 3 liang of Da Huang (rhubarb), steamed, sliced, and baked
  • 5 qian of Da Fu Zi (mature tetracera), pitted
  • 1 liang of Gan Jiang (dried ginger), processed
  • 1.5 liang of Bie Jia (tortoise shell), boiled in vinegar, then roasted yellow and stir-fried

Grind the above into powder. Take 1 large sheng of matured rice vinegar, first boil 4-5 jiao (measures), then mix with the powdered medicine, forming pills the size of a tung seed. Take 10 to 20 pills with warm vinegar or rice wine on an empty stomach, resulting in purging of accumulated matter resembling foul blood and rotten flesh juice.

Xiao Qi Xiang Pill: Heats the middle, relieves diaphragm, transforms accumulation, and harmonizes qi. Treats vomiting due to alcohol, qi blockage with food, and food accumulation.

Ingredients:

  • 8 liang of Gan Song (sweet branch)
  • 6 liang of Yi Zhi Ren (black cardamom)
  • 12 liang each of Xiang Fu (cyperus), Ding Xiang (clove bark), and Gan Cao (licorice) (processed)
  • 2 liang each of Peng Zhu (dandelion) and Sui Sha (sand)

Grind the above into powder, form into pills the size of a mung bean. Take 20 pills, which can be consumed with warm wine, ginger soup, or hot water.

Chong Wan: Treats worm accumulation.

Ingredients:

  • Hu Huang Lian (golden thread),
  • Wu Yi (various herbs),
  • Lei Wan (thunder ball),
  • He Shi (herb from crane),
  • Da Huang (rhubarb),
  • Shi Jun Zi (shizhizi),
  • Xi Hui (tin ash),
  • San Leng (three-edged),
  • Peng Zhu (dandelion),
  • Mu Xiang (costus),
  • Bing Lang (betel nut),
  • Qing Pi (green skin).

Grind the above into fine powder and form into pills for consumption.[96p]

　　桃仁煎 【《良方》，下同】 　治血瘕。　　桃仁　大黄炒　(石卜)硝各一两　蝱虫半两，炒黑　　右为末，以醇酢一中盏，煮三分，下前三味，不住手搅，煎至可丸，乃下(石卜)硝，丸如桐子大，不吃晚食五更初温酒下五丸，日午下秽物。如未见，再服。仍以调气血药补之。
